## In progress - v0.10.0 Missions window: vessel composition over time (first cut, playtesting)

- Goal (from 2026-05-25 design chat): show each vessel's COMPOSITION (controllers + crew) broken into intervals of compositional stability, as a nested tree. A node = a stable composition labeled with counts ("pod x1, probe x1, crew x3"); it branches at composition-change events; a stable composition that ends as a whole is a terminal leaf.
- **Rules agreed (refined 2026-05-25):** an interval ends only on a STRUCTURAL change (a controller separates: decouple / undock); part count never forces a subtree. A crew-only change (a kerbal EVAs) does NOT end the interval - the vessel keeps the same controllers, so the kerbal hangs off the interval it left during as a child leaf and the interval label shows the SURVIVING crew (so a pod that sheds one of three crew on EVA reads `pod x1, crew x2` with the departed kerbal as an EVA child, NOT two pod intervals). A composition stable until it ends as a whole (Destroyed/Recovered/intact) is a terminal interval, regardless of controller count (a `probe x2` booster that crashes intact is one leaf). Single atom (1 controller or 1 kerbal) = plain leaf; a stable multi-atom terminal expands one optional level into its atoms. Each node's [start,end] + start/end events are its interval; deeper rows are finer sub-intervals.
- **Data (all directly available, confirmed by investigation):** `Recording.Controllers` (ControllerInfo.type: CrewedPod/ProbeCore/ExternalSeat/KerbalEVA) gives controller counts per leg; `Recording.StartCrew` (per-trait) gives crew count; the fork tree (BranchPointType {Undock,EVA,JointBreak,Breakup}=split; {Dock,Board}=merge) gives the timing; `TerminalState` {Destroyed,Recovered}=terminal-as-a-whole. No controller-count inference needed.
- **Implementation (structural-interval model, rewritten 2026-05-25):** `MissionLeg` enriched with PodCount/ProbeCount/SeatCount/CrewCount (populated in `MissionStructureBuilder` from the Recording). Pure `MissionCompositionBuilder.Build(structure)` -> per top-level vessel, `BuildNode` walks the FULL continuation through-line of one physical vessel (env-split continuations + the vessel-continuation fork child) into one run, classifies each non-continuation branch child as a STRUCTURAL peel (a controller separated: any non-EVA child) or a CREW peel (an EVA kerbal), then splits the run timeline at the structural peels' UTs into intervals. Each interval's controllers = the start composition minus the structural peels removed at or before its start (correct even when a continuing recording's start-captured Controllers are stale, e.g. a pod that keeps its recording after the probe decouples), and its crew = the roster surviving at its END (start roster minus the kerbals who left by then). The survivor (next interval) is each interval's first child, then the peeled pieces (recursed); crew peels attach to the interval live when they left. `MissionCompositionNode` carries label/span/events/IsLeaf/IsAtom; sub-interval head ids are synthetic (`<headId>/seg<i>`) so only the through-line head carries the loop checkbox. Rendered in the Missions window by `DrawCompositionNode`/`DrawCompositionRow`, REPLACING the through-line body rows: the wide column holds "Vessel (composition)" or the atom name, the four existing columns hold the interval's start/end time + events.
- **Named crew leaves (done):** the roster now shows one named leaf per kerbal (`MissionLeg.CrewNames` threaded from `Recording.CrewEndStates` keys, sorted), falling back to a single `crew xN` atom only when names are not recorded. The interval labels still use counts (`crew x3`) for compactness; names appear only at the leaf level.
- **Crew count from names (done):** real saves carry `CrewEndStates` (named roster) but NO `StartCrew` per-trait node, so `CrewCount` was 0 and the launch showed `pod x1, probe x1` with no crew. `PopulateComposition` now falls back to `CrewNames.Count` when `StartCrew` is absent, so the launch reads `pod x1, probe x1, crew x3`.
- **StartCrew on tree roots (recorder fix, done):** root cause of the missing `StartCrew` was the `FlightRecorder.StartRecording` backstop: it forwarded the captured `Controllers` onto the always-tree-root recording (created before the crew snapshot exists) but never the captured `StartCrew`, so launch roots kept controllers and lost crew. Added `Recording.AdoptStartCrewIfEmpty` (mirrors `AdoptControllersIfEmpty`, no-overwrite) and the backstop now forwards `pendingStartCrew` too, so NEW recordings carry the per-trait `StartCrew` manifest. Existing recordings still rely on the `CrewEndStates` name-count fallback above (no migration, pre-1.0). 3 new `CrewManifestTests`. NOTE: `StartResources`/`StartInventory` have the identical tree-root backstop gap (also captured into `pending*` but not forwarded); left as a known follow-up since this change targeted crew.
- **Synthesized continuing remainder (subsumed by the structural-interval model):** the reported case (a stack whose probe separates as an ANCHORED controlled offshoot while the pod keeps the SAME recording, start-captured `Controllers` stays `[pod,probe]`, no recaptured continuation leg, so the builder only showed the peeled probe) is now handled uniformly: the structural peel splits the run timeline, and the survivor interval's controllers = start minus the peels removed so far (`pod x1, probe x1, crew x3` minus the probe -> `pod x1, crew x3`), whether or not a separate continuation recording exists. The old standalone `BuildRemainderNode` was removed.
- **Event-label fixes (2 playtest bugs, done):** (1) "Broke off" appeared where "Decoupled" was expected. The composition view's `BranchEventName` switched on the bare `BranchPointType`, but a deliberate decoupler firing and an accidental structural break are BOTH `BranchPointType.JointBreak` (and a separator can surface as `Undock`): only `BranchPoint.SplitCause`/`BreakupCause` distinguishes them. Threaded the cause onto `MissionLeg.OriginCause`/`EndCause` (set in `MissionStructureBuilder.BuildBranchLinks` from `bp.SplitCause ?? bp.BreakupCause`) and made `BranchEventName(type, cause)` switch on the cause first (DECOUPLE->"Decoupled", UNDOCK->"Undocked", CRASH->"Crashed", OVERHEAT->"Overheated", STRUCTURAL_FAILURE->"Broke up"), falling back to the type only when no cause is recorded. (2) A continuing pod after a probe decouple showed its start event as the LATER EVA fork it was recaptured at, and its interval started there too, leaving the post-decouple span unrepresented. Fixed by the structural-interval rewrite (above): the survivor pod now STARTS at the decouple (`Decoupled`) and SPANS the EVA as one interval labeled by the surviving crew (`pod x1, crew x2`), with the EVA kerbal hanging off the survivor (its own start event = `EVA`). The launch interval ends at the decouple (the first structural change), not the recording's terminal fork.
- **Remaining first-cut limitations (follow-ups):** intra-vessel crew transfers are not recorded so they do not appear; debris-only stage separations (no controller on the jettisoned stage) do not create an interval (controller/crew composition genuinely unchanged); merges (dock/board) handled simply via the visited guard, not yet nested richly; the now-unused through-line render methods (`DrawThroughLine`/`DrawThroughLineRow`/`DrawReferenceRow`/`StartEventText`/`EndEventText`) are kept temporarily pending playtest confirmation, then removable.
- **Tests:** `MissionCompositionTests` (11): label format, single-controller leaf, crewed multi-atom terminal, crew-count-from-names, env-split grouping, decouple branch (DECOUPLE cause -> "Decoupled"), stale-controller continuing survivor, EVA keeps-one-interval (surviving crew, kerbal hangs off), the full Kerbal X case (probe decouple then later EVA -> survivor starts at decouple, spans the EVA, label crew x2), empty. Full suite green (12552).
- **Status:** FIRST CUT deployed for playtest 2026-05-25.

---

## In progress - v0.10.0 Missions window: interval-level start/end trim (render a sub-segment of a mission, playtesting)

- Goal (2026-05-25 design chat): let a player render only PART of a mission - keep a peeled branch while dropping its trunk (only "Kerbal X Probe" after the separation), or start-trim a continuing vessel at a structural change (only the pod AFTER the decouple, not the launch/ascent). Cuts are always at STRUCTURAL composition changes (decouple / undock), never at EVA - which is exactly where the composition tree already splits intervals.
- **Doability (traced):** the recording data already supports rendering any segment in isolation. Mesh is self-contained per leg (each recording has its own start snapshot; `ApplyPartEvents` walks a cursor from index 0 and applies every event with `ut <= currentUT`, so a ghost entered mid-recording catches up the staged-down state - the decouple is applied so the probe is gone in the first frame). Position is self-contained for Absolute/body-fixed legs; Relative anchors resolve from the recorded trajectory, not a rendered ghost, and fail closed. The span clock has no launch/root assumption. INVARIANT: never purge a recording that is the Relative anchor of a kept downstream segment (we hide-from-render, data stays resident, so safe today).
- **Scope decision:** INTERVAL level (each structural segment of a vessel is its own toggle); deeper per-leg trim deferred.
- **Phase 1 (DONE, pure model, no callers yet):** `MissionCompositionNode` gained `OwnerHeadId` (the through-line head a structural interval belongs to - all of a vessel's intervals share it; a peeled branch is its own) + `IsSelectable` (true for intervals/branches, false for roster atoms). New `Mission.ExcludedIntervalKeys` (excluded interval HeadLegIds), persisted (`excludedInterval` values) + copied by `Clone`. New pure `MissionIntervalSelection.ComputeRenderWindows(roots, excludedKeys)` -> per-vessel `[StartUT,EndUT]` render window (min start / max end over a vessel's INCLUDED intervals; vessel absent when all its intervals are excluded; no cascade - intervals toggle independently). 6 new tests (full-window; exclude-launch start-trims the pod to the decouple; exclude-all drops the pod but keeps branches; only-probe; null). Full suite green (12566).
- **Phase 2 (DONE, UI):** every selectable composition row (interval / branch) now carries its own independent include checkbox bound to `Mission.ExcludedIntervalKeys` (no cascade - unchecking the launch interval keeps the post-decouple survivor checked); roster atoms carry none and grey with their owning interval. Replaced the through-line-head-only checkbox + the `MissionSelection` cascade in the composition render (`DrawCompositionNode`/`DrawCompositionRow`, call site dropped `includedHeads`/`view`). `MissionSelection` is now unused by the window + the builder (kept; still has its own tests).
- **Phase 3 (DONE, render):** `LoopUnit` gained a per-member render window (`MemberWindow` + `MemberStartUT`/`MemberEndUT`, null = full range so untrimmed missions are byte-identical). `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.TryBuildMissionUnit` now derives members + windows from `MissionIntervalSelection.ComputeRenderWindows(ExcludedIntervalKeys)` (vessel window intersected with each member's range; member dropped when empty; span = min/max trimmed; `BuildSignature` folds `ExcludedIntervalKeys`). The three scene drivers use the trimmed window: flight (`GhostPlaybackEngine.UpdateUnitMemberPlayback` overlap + span-clock branches + `TryResolveUnitMemberPlaybackUT` watch), Space Center (`ParsekKSC.UpdateUnitMemberKsc` overlap + span-clock), Tracking Station (`GhostPlaybackLogic.ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT`). The staged-down mesh comes for free from the existing `ApplyPartEvents` catch-up (events <= the trimmed start are applied on spawn, so a pod started at the decouple shows the probe already gone). Multi-vessel ASYMMETRIC trims (two kept vessels with different start-trims) are handled per member (each member's own window), so this is correct, not just span-level.
- **Trim-boundary puff suppression (done):** the catch-up that crosses the decouple at the trimmed start must not fire the decouple's transient puff (`SpawnPartPuffAtPart`, which is gated by `allowTransientEffects`; the permanent part-hide runs regardless). The FLIGHT engine was already silent: `PrimeLoadedGhostForPlaybackUT` (first spawn AND loop-cycle reuse) catches up with `allowTransientEffects: false` (`HiddenPrimeVisualPolicy`). The SPACE CENTER was NOT: `ParsekKSC` applied the spawn-frame `ApplyPartEvents` with the default `allowTransientEffects: true`, so it puffed the catch-up. Fixed by passing `allowTransientEffects: !justSpawned` on the just-spawned single-ghost frame and `!primaryCycleChanged` on the freshly-spawned overlap primary (older overlap ghosts were primed when they were the primary, so they keep effects on). Bonus: this also stops the latent puff when ANY KSC ghost first appears mid-trajectory; untrimmed ghosts spawning at their start catch up zero events, so it is a no-op there.
- **Tests:** +1 `MissionLoopUnitBuilderTests.Build_ExcludingLaunchInterval_StartTrimsSpanAndMemberWindow` (excluding "L" start-trims the span to 30 + member L's window to [30,120], peeled branches dropped); the fork-exclusion test migrated to `ExcludedIntervalKeys`. Full suite green (12567).
- **Watch-camera crash on dropping the WATCHED member (playtest 2026-05-25, two-part fix):** `logs/2026-05-25_2149...` then `..._2219_uncheck-all-segments-nre`. Toggling the composition checkboxes while WATCHING a member until it left the loop unit (e.g. unchecking all segments) flooded the log with stock NREs (`FlightGlobals.UpdateInformation`/`Sun`/`CrewHatchController`/`AmbienceControl`) and broke the camera. (a) First pass added `GhostPlaybackEngine.IsLoopUnitMember(index)` + a guard in `WatchModeController.FindWatchedGhostState` returning null when a loop-cycle watch's recording is no longer a member. That was necessary but INSUFFICIENT: the second log showed it firing too late - the watched probe had `terminal=Destroyed`, so when dropped the engine's `UpdatePlayback` fired `PlaybackCompleted(pastEffectiveEnd)` -> the policy started a 5s watch-HOLD on it and exploded/destroyed the ghost, latching the camera onto a destroyed transform (`actualTarget=null`) BEFORE the per-frame `FindWatchedGhostState` guard ran; the corruption then persisted (~36s, until scene exit). (b) Real fix: `ParsekFlight.DriveMissionLoopUnits`, right after `engine.SetLoopUnits` (which runs BEFORE `UpdatePlayback`), now exits watch the instant the watched loop-cycle member is no longer in the rebuilt unit (`WatchedLoopCycleIndex >= 0 && !cachedLoopUnits.IsMember(WatchedRecordingIndex)`). So the camera restores to the active vessel before the dropped ghost is torn down / exploded, and no hold ever latches it. The `FindWatchedGhostState` guard stays as defense in depth. Unity-bound, so playtest-validated; full suite green (12569).
- **Watch follows the CURRENT overlapping instance, not each new launch (playtest 2026-05-25, fixed):** when watching an overlapping looped mission the camera jumped to every new launch (every overlap cadence) instead of following one launch to orbit. Root cause: the engine's self-overlap branch drove the watch stage-handoff (`LogUnitTransitionIfChanged`) off the NEWEST instance's span-progress (`ComputeNewestMissionInstanceSpanLoopUT`), so a new launch's launch-stage became the "live member" and the camera retargeted back to it. Fix: when the player is watching an instance of this unit (`ctx.protectedLoopCycleIndex >= 0` and `ctx.protectedIndex` is a unit member) and that instance is still in flight, drive the handoff off the WATCHED instance's clock via the new pure `GhostPlaybackLogic.TryComputeMissionInstanceSpanLoopUT(..., cycle, ...)` (returns false before launch / after the span ends). When the watched instance ENDS (per the user's choice), it falls back to the newest instance and the existing `FindWatchedGhostState` cycle-lost fallback snaps the camera onto the newest in-flight launch (matches single-recording overlap). 2 new `MissionSpanClockTests` for the per-cycle helper; Unity-bound handoff is playtest-validated. Full suite green (12569).
- **Ride-along debris not bounded by the parent member's trimmed window (playtest 2026-05-25, fixed):** watching only a late segment (e.g. the pod after the decouple, launch interval unchecked) still showed the earlier launch-stage debris. The general trim-scoping is correct (`logs/2026-05-25_2230...` shows active ghost count tracks membership: 1 member -> 1 active; a non-member like the probe is suppressed), but the engine's ride-along DEBRIS path (`GhostPlaybackEngine.TryUpdateLoopSyncedDebris`, `ShouldSourceDebrisFromUnitSpan` branch) scheduled each debris off its OWN `traj.StartUT` (`scheduleStartUT = PhaseAnchorUT + (debris.StartUT - SpanStartUT)`), never bounded by the parent member's TRIMMED window - so when the parent is start-trimmed, debris jettisoned before the trim start still loop. Fix: suppress the ride-along debris when its jettison `traj.StartUT` falls OUTSIDE the parent member's trimmed window (`parentUnit.MemberStartUT/EndUT(parentIdx)`); untrimmed parents keep their full range so it is a no-op there. (NOTE: the log captured the survivor/bob/probe toggles but NOT the launch-interval toggle, so the exact reported state was not in it; the fix is confirmed against the CODE - the schedule formula provably ignores the trim - not against a captured failing frame.) Unity-bound debris path, so playtest-validated; full suite green (12569).
- **Watched vessel hands off to the EVA kerbal instead of the continuing craft (playtest 2026-05-25, fixed):** watching the Kerbal X pod, the segment did not run to its end (explosion); the Kerbal X Probe segment was fine because it has no fork. Root cause: at the EVA fork the pod's launch interval ends, and the unit's camera-live picker in `GhostPlaybackEngine.LogUnitTransitionIfChanged` chose the in-window member with the highest `StartUT`. The continuing pod (`cont`, VesselName "Kerbal X", StartUT 38.88) and the EVA kerbal (`Bob Kerman`, StartUT 38.88) tie, so the arbitrary tiebreak grabbed Bob; the camera followed Bob, who soon exceeded the ghost cutoff distance and exited watch, so the pod never ran to its explosion. Log evidence: `logs/2026-05-25_2241_kerbalx-watch-not-to-end` shows `Chain-loop unit owner=0 camera-live member #0->#11 at loopUT=38.89` and `unit watch retarget owner=0 member #0->#11 at loopUT=38.89` (#11 = Bob Kerman). Fix: made the live-member picker two-tier - a member whose VesselName matches the WATCHED member's VesselName (the continuing craft) always beats a non-match; within a tier, highest StartUT still wins. `watchedVesselName` is null when nothing is watched, so unwatched playback keeps the pure highest-StartUT behavior. Now watching the pod hands off launch-stage->upper-stage along the same craft (L->cont) instead of jumping to the EVA kerbal. Unity-bound watch path, so playtest-validated; full suite green (12569).
- **Watched vessel's explosion focus stolen by a surviving sibling at impact (playtest 2026-05-25, fixed):** after the watch-continuing-vessel fix above, watching the Kerbal X pod correctly followed it launch-stage -> upper-stage (#0 -> #10, both "Kerbal X"), but at the upper stage's impact the camera cut to the EVA kerbal (#11 "Bob Kerman") for a moment before returning to the active vessel, losing the explosion focus (and the upper-stage tail near impact felt cut short). Log evidence: `logs/2026-05-25_2253_kerbalx-upper-stage-gap` shows at loopUT 53.03 (the impact) `Explosion anchor clamp #10 ("Kerbal X") ... clearance=2.1m cycle=23` firing in the SAME frame as `unit watch retarget owner=0 member #10->#11` and `Ghost EXITED range: #10 cycle=23 (overlap expired)`. Root cause: when the watched member (#10, terminal=Destroyed) ended, the unit camera-live picker chose the only remaining in-window member (#11 Bob, a different vessel) and `LogUnitTransitionIfChanged` retargeted to it. The retarget runs BEFORE `UpdateOverlapPlayback` fires #10's `ExplosionHoldStart`, and `WatchModeController.HandleOverlapCameraAction` early-returns (`watchedRecordingIndex != evt.Index`) once the watch has moved to Bob, so the explosion hold for #10 was silently dropped and the camera jumped to Bob (who is far away and soon exits watch to the anchor). Fix: gate the unit handoff so the camera only follows a SAME-VESSEL continuation of the watched through-line. New pure `GhostPlaybackLogic.ResolveUnitHandoffRetargetMember(liveMemberIdx, liveMatchesWatched)` returns -1 when the chosen live member is a different vessel, suppressing the retarget; the watch then stays on the ending member so its own `ExplosionHoldStart` applies (camera holds on the explosion for `OverlapExplosionHoldSeconds`, then the existing post-hold retarget returns to the anchor / newest in-flight). Also extracted the two-tier picker comparison into pure `GhostPlaybackLogic.IsBetterUnitCameraLiveMember` (same vessel name beats highest StartUT). 6 new `MissionSpanClockTests` (picker tiers + retarget gating). Unity-bound watch path, so playtest-validated; full suite green (12575).
- **Watch loop restart: cross-instance jump + invalid post-hold position (playtest 2026-05-25, fixed):** two follow-ups to the explosion-hold fix, found in `logs/2026-05-25_2313_kerbalx-bob-toggle`. (1) **Bob UNCHECKED** (members=2, span=[29.56,53.02] so #10's end IS the span end): when the watched upper stage #10 ended, the watched-instance pin dropped (`TryComputeMissionInstanceSpanLoopUT` false at span end), the handoff fell back to the NEWEST instance, the picker found that instance's #0 (same vessel "Kerbal X"), and fired `unit watch retarget #10->#0 at loopUT=33.03` - a CROSS-INSTANCE jump to a fresh launch mid-#0 (after the capsule/tank separation) that ALSO preempted #10's explosion hold. (2) **Bob CHECKED** (members=3, span extended to 58.52 by Bob so #10 ends mid-span): the explosion hold fired correctly, but the post-hold retarget (`WatchModeController.TryResolveOverlapRetarget`) targeted `ghostStates[#10]` - the exploded upper stage's OWN newest cycle, which is relative-anchored and was `retired=true ... pos=(578577,542584,-95000)` (the "invalid position") before snapping back. Both want: hold the explosion, then RESTART at the mission start (#0, the launch stage). Fix: (a) suppress the unit handoff when the watched INSTANCE has ended (`watchedInstanceEnded = watchingThisUnitInstance && !watchPinnedToInstance`, threaded into `LogUnitTransitionIfChanged` as `suppressWatchRetarget`), so the cross-instance jump no longer preempts the hold; (b) post-hold, restart the camera on the unit's through-line ROOT via new `GhostPlaybackEngine.TryGetUnitThroughLineRoot` (returns `unit.OwnerIndex`, the earliest member = launch stage) + `TransferWatchToNextSegment(root)`, landing on a fresh #0 launch near the trimmed start (valid position) instead of the exploded #10's primary. Single-recording overlap watch is unaffected (`TryGetUnitThroughLineRoot` returns false for non-unit-members, keeping the existing primary retarget). Unity-bound watch path, so playtest-validated; full suite green (12575).
- **Relative-to-sibling section retired with no body-fixed fallback -> gap + invisible kerbal + 798 km camera jump (playtest 2026-05-25, TWO commits):** watching the Kerbal X mission, the upper stage "jumped from the EVA moment to later" (a ~14 s gap), Bob (the EVA kerbal) was never visible, and the watch camera jumped ~798 km away. Diagnosis from `logs/2026-05-25_2334` then `..._2354`: the upper stage #10 (fc0ebaca "Kerbal X", terminal=Destroyed) recorded its mid-section [38.96, 48.46] `ref=Relative` anchored to the probe #8 (f9df712d), which decoupled and crashed ~0.1 s after the EVA. So #10's recorded section anchor ran out almost immediately and #10 showed `reason=resolver-miss-or-retired retired=true active=false` for most of its window, frozen at a garbage position. Bob #11 is anchored to #10, so it inherited the garbage pos -> `anchorDist=4023m renderDist=798118m` -> hidden by distance LOD; the watch camera (following #10) jumped to the garbage pos (~798 km). #10's section HAS 45 valid body-fixed points covering [38.96, 48.44] (confirmed in the .prec), so the data to render it correctly was present the whole time.
  - **Commit 1 (necessary but NOT the fix):** the LOOP path `PositionLoopAtPlaybackUT` gated the body-fixed-primary route on `traj.IsDebris && ParentAnchorRecordingId != null` while the NON-loop path used `ParentAnchorRecordingId != null` alone. Extracted the shared gate `GhostPlaybackEngine.IsParentAnchoredBodyFixedPrimaryCandidate` (= `ParentAnchorRecordingId != null`) and used it in both paths so they can't diverge. This did NOT fix #10 because #10 is a TOP-LEVEL vessel: `ParentAnchorRecordingId == null` (only the SECTION carries `anchorRecordingId`; the recording is not parent-anchored). Still a real consistency fix (a genuine controlled-decoupled child WOULD have hit it).
  - **Commit 2 (the actual fix):** the body-fixed fallback after the relative positioner in BOTH `PositionLoopAtPlaybackUT` and `TryPositionRelativeSectionAtPlaybackUT` was gated on `parentAnchored && loopAnchoredDebrisChain`, so a top-level vessel whose active Relative section's anchor retired had no fallback and stayed retired. Broadened it to fire whenever `state.anchorRetiredThisFrame` is set: `TryPositionBodyFixedPrimary` is self-gating (only succeeds when the active section is Relative AND its bodyFixedFrames cover the UT), so it is inert for absolute sections / sections without a body-fixed surface, and otherwise the ghost plays its own recorded body-fixed track instead of vanishing. Bob (anchored to #10) then resolves near #10 and the watch camera stays on #10's real position. 5 new `GhostPlaybackEngineTests` total (3 gate + 2 top-level-relative fallback, incl. the no-body-fixed negative). Unity-bound playback path, so playtest-validated; full suite green (12580).
- **Parent-anchored child's ABSOLUTE section force-retired in the LOOP path -> "Kerbal X Probe was not watchable" (playtest 2026-05-26, fixed):** the probe #8 (f9df712d "Kerbal X Probe") entered watch but its ghost never rendered (all 13688 frames `retired=true active=false`), so the camera immediately dropped back. Diagnosis from `logs/2026-05-26_0015`: the probe IS parent-anchored (`ParentAnchorRecordingId` set in tree metadata, NOT the .prec - which is why `IsParentAnchoredBodyFixedPrimaryCandidate` returns true), and it is a controlled-decoupled child (`IsDebris=false`) whose ONLY section [30.10, 48.46] is `ref=Absolute src=Background` with `bodyFixedFrames=0`. The retire log was the smoking gun: `recorded-relative-retired coverageReason=body-fixed-primary-position-failed recording=#8 callsite=...UpdateOverlapPlayback.primary`. Root cause: `PositionLoopAtPlaybackUT` forced the body-fixed-primary route for ANY parent-anchored recording regardless of whether the ACTIVE section was Relative - but `TryPositionBodyFixedPrimary`/`BodyFixedPrimaryCoversPlaybackUT` only succeed for a Relative section, so the probe's Absolute section failed the route and line 4701 retired it every frame. The NON-loop path `TryPositionRelativeSectionAtPlaybackUT` already bails out for Absolute sections via `TryGetRelativeSectionAtUT` (returns false -> caller uses the normal absolute path); the loop path lacked the equivalent gate (same loop/non-loop divergence as the prior two fixes). Fix: gate the loop path's body-fixed-primary route + retire on `activeSectionIsRelative = TryGetRelativeSectionAtUT(traj, loopUT, out _)`, so a parent-anchored child whose current section is Absolute (its post-decouple tail) falls through to the normal absolute loop positioner. 1 new `GhostPlaybackEngineTests.PositionLoopAtPlaybackUT_ParentAnchoredChildAbsoluteSection_UsesAbsoluteLoopNotBodyFixed`. Unity-bound playback path, so playtest-validated; full suite green (12581).
- **Ride-along debris overlap list wiped every frame -> debris vanishes after one loop period (playtest 2026-05-26, fixed):** a jettisoned booster ("Jumping Flea Debris", recorded jettison ~UT 20 -> ocean crash/Destroyed at UT 42, ~22s) was visible for only ~one loop period in the looped mission, never falling all the way to its crash. Diagnosis: added a non-gated per-frame visibility log (`GhostPlaybackEngine.LogLoopSyncedDebrisOverlapVisibility`) because `GhostRenderTrace` only logs ~4s after each spawn (`InitialWindowSeconds=4.0`) - which earlier produced a misleading "5s clip" read - and `overlap-move` uses a SHARED rate-limit key, so its absence for one index proves nothing. The new log showed `overlapActive=0/0` every frame while `newestLoopUT` swept ~20->30 (one cadence) then reset, with `GetActiveCycles` reporting 3 cycles should be live. Root cause: `GhostPlaybackEngine.UpdatePlayback`'s per-trajectory loop ran the "clean up overlap ghosts if recording switched from looping to non-looping" block (`DestroyAllOverlapGhosts(i); overlapGhosts.Remove(i);`) BEFORE `TryUpdateLoopSyncedDebris`. A ride-along debris renders through the overlap path (`UpdateOverlapPlayback` owns `overlapGhosts[i]`), so the cleanup destroyed each demoted background instance (the older debris pieces still coasting to the ocean) the frame after it was demoted - leaving only the freshest instance, which resets every cadence and never plays its full arc. Unit members (`#0`) and per-recording-looping ghosts dispatch + `continue` earlier so they never hit the cleanup, which is why the parent demoted fine and only the debris broke. Fix: run `TryUpdateLoopSyncedDebris` BEFORE the loop->non-loop overlap cleanup; the cleanup is now reached only by genuinely non-looping recordings (a debris whose parent stopped looping returns false and still gets its stale overlaps cleared). Kept the visibility diagnostic (rate-limited 2s) to confirm `overlapActive>0` post-fix. Unity-bound playback path, so playtest-validated; full suite green (12585).
- **Looped mission's MAP orbit lines + icons wrong/stale/missing in flight map view AND the Tracking Station (playtest 2026-05-26, fixed):** in-flight ghost MESHES looped correctly (engine `path=loop-overlap`), but the map-view ProtoVessels (orbit lines + icons) did not. Diagnosed from `logs/2026-05-26_2222`: the orbital members (#5 "Kerbal X", #13 "Kerbal X Probe") sat `Deferred ... recording starts pre-orbital` and never materialized. **Two coupled defects.** (1) **Flight map view had no loop clock at all:** `ParsekPlaybackPolicy.CheckPendingMapVessels` sampled segments/points + made create/defer/remove decisions at the raw live `currentUT` (sites at the pending-create, 2a segment-update, and 2b state-vector loops), with no `LoopUnitSet` - so for a looped member living at recorded UT `[3991,54028]` while the clock was ~62000 it picked the wrong segment or none. TS (`UpdateTrackingStationGhostLifecycle`) and KSC already remap via `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT`; flight never got the equivalent. (2) **Icon PHASE wrong in all map scenes:** the map icon renders at `orbit.getPositionAtUT(liveUT)` propagated from the seeded epoch; TS/KSC (and the new flight path) seed the orbit at the loop-mapped `effUT`, so an orbital member's icon propagated `(liveUT - effUT)` (up to >1 orbit for the ~10.7h-period probe) and landed at an arbitrary phase. Not caught earlier because the KSC/TS phases were validated on suborbital members (atmospheric markers draw straight from world position, not orbit-propagated). **Fix (uniform, all scenes):** added `loopEpochShiftSeconds = liveUT - effUT` (default 0, so non-loop is byte-identical) to the shared seed path - `GhostMapPresence.UpdateGhostOrbitFromStateVectors` (reseed epoch = `ut + shift`) and `ApplyOrbitToVessel`/`UpdateGhostOrbitForRecording` (SetOrbit epoch = `segment.epoch + shift` AND stored `ghostOrbitBounds` shifted by the same amount, so the arc-clip / icon-clamp Harmony patches in `GhostOrbitLinePatch.cs`, which compare live `Planetarium` time against the bounds in recorded UT, stay aligned). The shift is constant within a loop cycle (effUT tracks liveUT 1:1), so natural orbit propagation between the rate-limited reseeds matches the replay and it only re-snaps at a cycle wrap. Threaded `engine.CurrentLoopUnits` (new accessor on `GhostPlaybackEngine`) into `CheckPendingMapVessels` via the new `ResolveMapPresenceSampleUT` helper (substitutes `effUT` at every sample/decide site; `renderHidden` tears the ghost down + re-defers, mirroring the TS refresh pass) and passes the matching shift to the seed calls; TS `RefreshTrackingStationGhosts` now passes `liveUT - effUT` to its state-vector + segment applies. KSC needs no change (it renders physical meshes, not orbit-propagated map icons). 3 new `MissionSpanClockTests` pin the shift arithmetic (non-member 0, wrapped cycle = one cadence, anchored = liveUT - spanStart); the Unity orbit math is playtest-validated. Full suite green (12586). **Clean Opus review follow-up:** the reviewer flagged that `TryGetVisibleOrbitBoundsForGhostVessel` re-derives bounds from the RAW recorded OrbitSegments at the raw live UT before falling back to the stored (shifted) `ghostOrbitBounds` - so if the live clock ever falls INSIDE a looped member's recorded UT window (reachable via rewind / warp-to-time), it would hand the arc/icon patches raw recorded bounds against a shifted orbit epoch and mis-clip. Hardened with a `ghostOrbitLoopShiftedPids` set (marked/unmarked in `ApplyOrbitToVessel` by `loopEpochShiftSeconds != 0`, cleared alongside `ghostOrbitBounds`): for a loop-shifted ghost the resolver returns the stored shifted bounds directly instead of re-deriving. Empty off the loop path, so non-loop bounds resolution is unchanged. Review verdict was SHIP-WITH-FIXES (this edge + two comment-accuracy nits, both addressed); full suite still green (12589).
- **Status:** deployed for playtest 2026-05-26 (watch-crash + watch-follow-current-instance + debris-trim-bound + watch-continuing-vessel + watched-explosion-hold + watch-loop-restart + relative-anchor-retired-body-fixed-fallback + parent-anchored-absolute-section-loop + ride-along-debris-overlap-wipe + map-presence-loop-clock-and-icon-phase fixes in the same session). Ghost-marker right-click + opacity + TS-popup-dismiss-on-press fixes added 2026-05-27.
- **Tracking Station looped-mission orbit freezes on the parking orbit after launch (playtest 2026-05-27, fixed):** the non-protovessel icon tracked the atmo-exit correctly, but once the looped Mun mission's replay left the Kerbin parking orbit, the TS proto-vessel orbit + icon stuck on the parking ellipse and never advanced through the transfer / Mun phases (the orbit "disappeared" once the live clock ran past the frozen, shifted parking-orbit bounds). Diagnosed from `logs/2026-05-27_2210_ts-protovessel-disappear`: member #15 (`7f4427...` "Kerbal X", 8 OrbitSegments spanning parking orbit -> trans-Munar transfer -> Mun terminal orbit) was created from `Segment` (parking orbit `[4181.1,4779.4]`), but the moment `effUT` advanced into the transfer phase (recorded as `ref=OrbitalCheckpoint` sections) the per-tick update logged `update-state-vector-skip ... branch=OrbitalCheckpoint reason=state-vector-from-orbital-checkpoint` and `UpdateGhostOrbitFromStateVectors` returned false (neither updated nor removed), freezing the orbit. **Root cause (flight-vs-TS asymmetry):** the TS update path `GhostMapPresence.RefreshTrackingStationGhosts` re-derives `fromCheckpoint` from the section covering `effUT` EVERY tick and checks it BEFORE the OrbitSegment path, so a Segment-created ghost was misrouted into the distrusted OrbitalCheckpoint state-vector refusal (which is correctly refused with `allowOrbitalCheckpointStateVector=false`, but should not have been consulted at all). The create-path `ResolveTrackingStationGhostSource` and the flight-scene `ParsekPlaybackPolicy.CheckPendingMapVessels` both PREFER a wrapped/closed OrbitSegment covering the UT and only use the checkpoint state-vector as a genuine-segment-gap fallback; the TS update path violated that precedence. **Fix:** in `RefreshTrackingStationGhosts`, compute `coveringSegment = TrajectoryMath.FindOrbitSegmentForMapDisplay(rec.OrbitSegments, effUT)` once and gate the checkpoint branch on the new pure `GhostMapPresence.ShouldConsumeCheckpointStateVectorForExistingGhost(fromCheckpoint, segmentCoversEffUT)` (= `fromCheckpoint && !segmentCoversEffUT`), so a covering OrbitSegment wins and the ghost falls through to the segment update path (which advances through the transfer ellipse + Mun orbit, shifted into the live frame by `tsLoopEpochShift`). The checkpoint state-vector stays available only for a real segment gap (no covering segment at `effUT`), matching the create / flight precedence. The segment path reuses `coveringSegment` (no double `FindOrbitSegmentForMapDisplay`). A rate-limited `ts-checkpoint-defer-to-segment` Verbose line confirms the guard fires for a looped ghost crossing from parking orbit into a transfer OrbitalCheckpoint section. New `GhostMapSoiGapStateVectorTests.ShouldConsumeCheckpointStateVectorForExistingGhost_PrefersCoveringSegment` (4-case truth table). Unity-bound TS path, so playtest-validated; full suite green (12651).
- **Follow-up (playtest 2026-05-27, `logs/2026-05-27_2249_ts-proto-misposition`): TS looped orbit jumped to the terminal Mun orbit during the transfer + suppressed the non-proto marker.** After the checkpoint-precedence fix the freeze was gone, but the user saw the proto-vessel orbit reseed onto the FINAL Mun orbit the instant it left the parking orbit (mispositioned, camera pulled to the Mun on an eccentric ~suborbital-looking orbit), and the non-proto position marker never drew for the transfer burn. Root cause: this recording's transfer phase ([4779, ~24000]) has NO covering `OrbitSegment` (`FindOrbitSegmentForMapDisplay` only ever returns the parking orbit `[4181,4779]` or the synthetic endpoint tail), so once effUT passed the parking orbit the TS segment path hit `!seg.HasValue` and the endpoint-tail (terminal-orbit) fallback fired. `IsTerminalMapPresenceRegion` is true for the WHOLE post-launch replay of an orbit-terminating recording (not just near the end), so the fallback wrongly reseeded the looped proto-vessel onto the terminal Mun orbit (sma 202914, ecc 0.785) for the entire rest of the replay; the surviving ghost then made `ClassifyAtmosphericMarkerSkip` return `NativeIconActive`, suppressing the atmospheric position marker. The create path already returns None (`before-terminal-orbit`) mid-recording when there is track coverage, so it never recreates the ghost in the gap; only the UPDATE path's endpoint-tail branch was at fault. The flight scene (`CheckPendingMapVessels`) avoids this with a `hasFutureSegment` check: a mid-recording gap removes the proto-vessel (`gap-between-orbit-segments`) rather than showing the terminal orbit. **Fix:** new pure `GhostMapPresence.HasOrbitSegmentStartingAfter(segments, effUT)`; in the TS segment path gate the `!seg.HasValue` endpoint-tail branch on `!hasFutureOrbitSegment` and, when a future segment exists, remove the proto-vessel with `gap-between-orbit-segments` instead of `tracking-station-expired`. The endpoint tail stays reserved for the genuine terminal region (no future segment). Once removed, the non-proto atmospheric marker draws the transfer/coast position (`ClassifyAtmosphericMarkerSkip` -> None since no ghost and not in an orbit segment), and the create pass re-materializes the orbit at the next real segment (the destination Mun orbit). This addresses BOTH reported symptoms (mispositioned proto orbit + camera jump to the Mun, and the missing propulsive-phase marker). New `GhostMapSoiGapStateVectorTests.HasOrbitSegmentStartingAfter_DetectsMidRecordingGapVsTerminal`. Unity-bound TS path, so playtest-validated; full suite green (12652).
- **Follow-up (playtest 2026-05-27, `logs/2026-05-27_2313_mun-soi-render`): TS looped orbit jumped to the terminal Mun orbit at ~181 Mm during the Mun APPROACH (flight rendered it correctly).** With the gap + checkpoint fixes deployed, the launch / parking-orbit / transfer-ellipse phases rendered correctly in BOTH scenes, but in the TS the Mun-approach phase put the proto orbit ~181,000,000 m from origin (off in empty space, ~15x the Mun's ~12 Mm distance) for the few seconds the brief Mun phase replayed; flight placed the same orbit at ~10-11.5 Mm (correct), so a flight-correct / TS-wrong asymmetry. Diagnosed: the chained Kerbin->Mun "Kerbal X" link #15 (`7f4427`) enters Mun SOI at effUT ~20094 (end of the transfer ellipse), so its segments past that are Mun (`20094-22523`, `22527-25638`, `25672-26717`, `27772-27888`). At effUT ~24656 (liveUT 1275515 - loop epoch shift 1250859) the covering Mun segment `22527-25638` was correctly found, but the TS update path's FIRST endpoint-tail branch (`ShouldOverrideVisibleSegmentWithEndpointTail`) overrode it: that predicate flags any terminal-body segment ending before the tail UT (27895) as "stale" and replaces it with the synthetic endpoint-tail seeded from the recording's recorded historical Mun lat/lon/rotation (`OrbitReseed.TryFromHistoricalLatLonAltAndRecordedVelocity`). That historical-absolute seed does not survive the loop epoch shift for a cross-body terminal (the Mun's RECORDED position != its live position), landing the orbit ~181 Mm off. The flight scene's segment-update path (`CheckPendingMapVessels` 2a) renders the covering segment directly and never applies that override, which is why flight was correct. **Fix:** the endpoint-tail is a NON-loop concept (it shows where a finished flight ended up); a loop member's effUT is always inside the recording, so its covering OrbitSegment is the correct current orbit and must always win. Suppress BOTH endpoint-tail branches in the TS update path for loop members (`isLoopMember = tsLoopEpochShift != 0.0`): a loop member renders real covering segments (the real terminal Mun orbit segment `27772-27888` shows correctly), and a no-covering-segment gap removes the proto-vessel (atmospheric marker + next-cycle re-materialization), exactly like flight. Non-loop members keep the full endpoint-tail behavior (the `!hasFutureOrbitSegment` gate still governs them). Same-body (e.g. Kerbin-orbit) loop members are unaffected because their terminal orbit is a real covering segment. Full suite green (12652); playtest pending.
- **Verified fixed + two DEFERRED items (playtest 2026-05-27, `logs/2026-05-27_2348_mun-takeoff-sync`; user chose "leave as-is for now").** Re-checked after the loop-member endpoint-tail suppression: the 181 Mm misplacement is GONE (idx 15's Mun endpoint-tail now seeds at ~11.3 Mm, correct) and there are NO crashes/NREs after the Mun takeoff (only the expected `MissionPeriodicity` Tier-1 residual warning). Root reality surfaced while investigating: this mission's chain links are recorded almost entirely via the section-authoritative path with `rebuiltOrbitSegments=0` (ascent, the Mun descent/landing/takeoff, AND the post-takeoff "Orbiting" return link #18); only link #15 (the Kerbin->Mun arc, 8 segments) and the probe carry real `OrbitSegment` map-line geometry. So most of the looped mission can only render as point markers, and the map is inherently a mix of a few orbit-line arcs (#15) + many point markers. ~~**Deferred item A (visual enhancement):** the orbit-line arcs and the propulsive/suborbital point markers do not connect end-to-end (a point can't continue an arc); the real "sync" fix is a NEW map-view ghost trajectory POLYLINE drawn through the recorded points for non-orbital phases, bridging the arcs (own feature/commit; inter-body phase-alignment caveats still apply to where the Mun arcs sit).~~ **Fixed**: `Source/Parsek/Display/GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.cs` adds a DDOL Vectrosity Driver that walks `RecordingStore.CommittedRecordings` per frame (always on; there is no user setting, no persistence, and no CustomParameterUI -- the polyline is permanently visible), builds one `LineType.Continuous` VectorLine PER non-orbital leg (cap 200 points / leg, endpoints preserved) and draws each leg full-range as a SOLID orbit-style line via `MapView.OrbitLinesMaterial`. (A single shared per-recording line drawn once per leg via `drawStart`/`drawEnd` range slicing does NOT work: `VectorLine.Draw3D()` zeroes every vertex outside the current `[drawStart, drawEnd]` window on each call, so only the last leg would survive; each leg owns its own line, and all per-leg lines are destroyed on cache refresh / release / clear so no Vectrosity GameObjects leak.) **Geometry contract:** the pure builder downsamples + caps each leg into raw `(lat, lon, alt)` triples ONLY (xUnit-testable, no KSP conversion); the Driver does the world conversion at draw time via `body.GetWorldSurfacePosition(lat, lon, alt)` -> `ScaledSpace.LocalToScaledSpace`, mirroring `ParsekTrackingStation.cs:1199` so the polyline lands exactly where the atmospheric markers land (the earlier `SphericalToBodyLocal` test fixture with a hard-coded 600 km radius was removed from production). Per-section dispatch picks `section.frames` for Absolute, `section.bodyFixedFrames` for Relative (skips Relative-without-bodyFixed to avoid the CLAUDE.md anchor-local-as-lat/lon footgun), plus flat `Recording.Points` outside any section. All collected non-orbital samples are then UT-sorted and MERGED into one leg per contiguous span, splitting only on a body change or an OrbitSegment coast falling between two samples (`ShouldDrawLegAtHeadUT` / `OrbitalIntervalBetween`). This is because the recorder fragments a single burn into many short env-class sections (e.g. the Kerbin circularization and the trans-Munar relight each split into 5-7 sub-second ExoBallistic<->ExoPropulsive sections); one-leg-per-section plus the head-UT draw gate showed only a short stub under the head, so a burn "fell short". Merging makes the whole burn render as one continuous line from the previous orbit arc to the next. **Visibility:** the Driver applies STATIC recording-level filters (`ClassifyPolylineStaticSkip`: debris, no committed trajectory, suppression) plus `renderHidden` / loop-unit visibility, and then a per-LEG head-UT gate (`ShouldDrawLegAtHeadUT`): each leg draws only while the ghost's current playback position (the `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT` return, `loopUT` for loop members else `liveUT`) lies within that leg's recorded `[startUT, endUT]`, so the polyline follows the ghost through its current non-orbital phase and hands off to the orbit arc during orbital phases instead of painting the whole recorded path at once (this is also why a multi-leg recording near the Mun no longer shows several overlapping legs at once). It deliberately does NOT use the `ClassifyAtmosphericMarkerSkip` per-head-UT RECORDING gate (which would blink the whole recording's polyline out the moment any ghost ProtoVessel / orbit line exists). A per-frame deactivation sweep sets `vectorLine.active = false` on any cached leg NOT drawn this frame (head-UT-gated out / loop-hidden / suppressed / body-missing / recording removed from `CommittedRecordings`), and the feature-OFF path deactivates all cached lines, because `VectorLine.Draw3D()` is one-shot and never hides a line on its own (mirrors `GhostOrbitLinePatch`'s `line.active` toggling); the sweep decision is the pure `ShouldDeactivateLeg`. While the polyline draws a recording's non-orbital leg the Driver publishes that RecordingId (`IsRenderingNonOrbitalLeg`), and `GhostOrbitLinePatch.Postfix` (on `OrbitRendererBase.LateUpdate`) hides that ghost's proto-vessel orbit LINE for the frame via `line.active = false` (resolving pid -> RecordingId through `GhostMapPresence.IsPolylineOwningGhostPhase` / `vesselPidToRecordingId`). Without it the proto-vessel orbit was never hidden during non-orbital phases (`rendererEnabled=True` for all updates, churning every ~0.5 s under warp) and lingered on top of the polyline. The renderer is left ENABLED (only `line.active` is toggled, the same idiom the patch uses for atmosphere / out-of-bounds suppression), so the Postfix keeps running every frame and re-shows the line automatically the moment the polyline relinquishes the phase. During the suppressed phase the proto-vessel ICON is also hidden (`drawIcons = NONE` + `ghostsWithSuppressedIcon.Add`, matching the below-atmosphere branch), so the non-proto trajectory marker (which `ClassifyAtmosphericMarkerSkip` draws only when the proto icon is suppressed) is the SOLE position indicator; keeping the proto icon (OBJ) drew BOTH it and the non-proto marker (the overlapping icons seen in playtest, since `GhostOrbitIconClampPatch` already suppresses the off-arc icon during non-orbital phases, which un-skips the marker). To guarantee that single marker actually draws everywhere, BOTH marker paths (`ParsekUI.DrawMapMarkers` in flight + `ClassifyAtmosphericMarkerSkip` in the TS) treat `GhostMapPresence.IsPolylineOwningGhostPhase(pid)` as "native proto icon not visible" (checked directly, not via the icon-suppressed flag, which `GhostOrbitIconClampPatch` can clear on-arc). Without this the non-proto marker was skipped as `NativeIconActive` while the proto icon was hidden, so an AIRLESS descent (the Mun) rendered the polyline with NO ghost icon at all. This runs identically in flight and the Tracking Station (driven by the renderer's own LateUpdate, not the throttled orbit-updater cadence), and is a no-op whenever the polyline is not drawing (the published set is empty -- e.g. not in map view or wrong scene). An earlier attempt that disabled `orbitRenderer.enabled` from the orbit updaters was wrong (a disabled renderer never re-enabled on a same-body burn, and reusing the state-vector updater's `return true` tore the proto-vessel down every tick) and was replaced by this patch-side `line.active` approach per the clean-context review. The Driver carries `[DefaultExecutionOrder(-50)]` so its `LateUpdate` publishes `activeLegRecordings` BEFORE stock `OrbitRendererBase.LateUpdate` (order 0) reads it through the patch; without it the patch read the previous frame's set, so at a burn's first frame it still drew the prior orbit arc while the polyline drew the burn (confirmed during bring-up by a temporary `RENDER OVERLAP` detector, since removed). Forcing the order is safe because `cachedLoopUnits` is computed in the scene controllers' `Update()`, which always precedes every `LateUpdate`. A second handoff artifact (the orbit re-showing the PREVIOUS segment's arc for ~0.5 s before the per-frame reseed catches up at a burn END) is fixed by a stale-segment guard in `GhostOrbitLinePatch`: when the polyline feature is on and the proto-vessel's applied orbit segment (`TryGetVisibleOrbitBoundsForGhostVessel`) no longer covers the head UT, the line stays hidden (`stale-segment-awaiting-reseed`, non-proto marker covers the gap) until the reseed updates the segment, so only the correct orbit is ever drawn (the always-on polyline owns the burn, so this guard always applies). Line style: a SOLID continuous line that mirrors the stock map orbit line exactly (`MapView.OrbitLinesMaterial`, 5px width, same `_FadeStrength` / `_FadeSign` distance fade as `OrbitRendererBase.MakeLine`), coloured the EXACT stock vessel orbit-line grey (KSP's `OrbitRenderer` seeds an unfocused vessel with `SetColor(new Color(0.71,0.71,0.71,1))` and draws the line at `orbitColor = nodeColor * 0.5` with `lineOpacity=1`, i.e. mid-grey) via a per-line vertex colour so it matches the ghost's own orbit arcs without mutating the shared material; an earlier dotted/dashed `MapView.DottedLinesMaterial` style read as a thick feathered brush stroke and was dropped. Each leg's VectorLine transform is zeroed every frame (`rectTransform.position = Vector3.zero`, plus identity rotation / unit scale, mirroring `OrbitRendererBase`'s REDRAW path) because the `points3` are ABSOLUTE ScaledSpace positions; without it the mesh inherits its parent/canvas transform and visibly drifts as the map camera pans instead of staying fixed in space. Per-scene controller refs and a name->CelestialBody map are cached and re-resolved only on scene change / null. Cache invariant is a cheap XOR-of-UTs content hash; `GameEvents.onGameStateLoad` flushes the cache across save/load. Plan: `docs/dev/plans/map-trajectory-polyline.md`. ~~**Deferred item B (regression trade-off from the endpoint-tail suppression):** a loop member that is `terminal=Orbiting` but has NO recorded `OrbitSegment`s (e.g. #18, the same-body Kerbin-return after the Mun takeoff) now shows a point marker instead of a synthesized terminal-orbit line, because the suppression covers BOTH endpoint-tail branches. A refinement would keep the no-covering-segment terminal fallback (SECOND branch) for loop members while keeping the covering-segment override (FIRST branch, the actual 181 Mm bug) suppressed - but that risks reintroducing the cross-body misplacement for a segment-less cross-body terminal, so it needs care. Both deferred per the user; the 181 Mm + freeze + camera-jump bugs that motivated the work are fixed.~~ **(Fixed 2026-05-28, plan v5 `docs/dev/plans/fix-terminal-orbit-for-loop-members.md`.)** The refinement is implemented: a same-body loop terminal (last-point body matches `TerminalOrbitBody`) re-enables the no-covering-segment SECOND endpoint-tail branch in the TS refresh path AND the create-path terminal-orbit fallback, while the FIRST branch (covering-segment override, the 181 Mm bug class) stays unconditionally suppressed for loop members; cross-body loop terminals still suppress via the same-body predicate. Threaded behind `acceptTerminalOrbitSource` / `acceptTerminalOrbitForLoopSynthesis`, computed from `(loopEpochShiftSeconds != 0) && IsTerminalOrbitSynthesisSafeForLoopMember(traj)`; non-loop callers pass false (byte-identical). 18 new xUnit tests in `TerminalOrbitLoopSynthesisTests`.
- **Looped mission leg with a persisted real terminal vessel showed NO map trajectory during its window (playtest 2026-05-29, `logs/2026-05-29_2351_munt-takeoff-no-traj`, fixed):** the Mun-return leg #18 (`80d467bc...`, terminal=Orbiting Kerbin) rendered nothing in the flight map view through its whole replay window (loopUT `[28212,47424]`), and the per-frame pending-create logged thousands of `IsTerminalOrbitSynthesisSafeForLoopMember` / `Pending map-create accepting terminal-orbit synthesis` lines (5212 in the capture). **Root cause (confirmed from the save):** recording #18 carries `spawnedPid = 2180236172`, a real "Kerbal X" Ship still ORBITING Kerbin (SMA 11.0 Mm) left over from the original mission flight. `IsMaterializedForMapPresence(#18)` returns true via `SpawnedVesselPersistentId != 0` (+ the real vessel existing), so the `alreadyMaterialized` early-return in `GhostMapPresence.ResolveMapPresenceGhostSource` (which precedes ALL segment / terminal-orbit logic) returned `source=None reason=already-spawned` every frame. The looped ghost never got an animated map orbit (the static real vessel sat at the FINAL Kerbin orbit, far from where the ghost was actually flying), and #18 stayed stuck in `pendingMapVessels` forever (never created, never removed), causing the per-frame log spam. The deferred-item-B terminal-orbit synthesis was bypassed entirely because the materialized gate short-circuits before it; the plan assumed #18 was a no-segment recording with no spawned vessel, but the real #18 has 6 OrbitSegments AND a persisted real vessel. **Fix (user decision: "draw ghost alongside real vessel"):** a Mission-loop member replaying inside its window draws its map ghost even when a persisted real terminal vessel exists (both icons may show). Added a `loopMemberInWindow` flag (computed from `loopEpochShift != 0`) threaded into `ResolveMapPresenceGhostSource` (gates the `alreadyMaterialized` early-return), `ResolveTrackingStationGhostSourceCore`, and `GetTrackingStationGhostRemovalReason` (so the next TS refresh tick does not tear the freshly-created ghost down again). Applied at all five loop-aware call sites: flight pending-create + SOI-gap update + terminal fallback (`ParsekPlaybackPolicy`), and the TS lifecycle create + refresh removal (`GhostMapPresence`). Re-fly / active-session duplicates stay blocked because `isSuppressed` is checked before the materialized gate. The new ghost ProtoVessel gets its own synthetic pid (`ghostMapVesselPids`), distinct from the real vessel's, so there is no identity collision. Log spam fixed separately: `IsTerminalOrbitSynthesisSafeForLoopMember` and the pending-accept line are now `VerboseRateLimited` (per-recording key). 2 new `GhostMapPresenceTests`. **Still open:** the warp-toggle icon jump the user also reported in this session is not yet pinned to a frame; re-check after this fix and capture the toggle moments if it persists.
- **Ghost trajectory polyline invisible in the Tracking Station (playtest 2026-05-30, `logs/2026-05-30_0032_ts-polyline-missing`, fixed):** the launch->Mun-landing non-orbital polylines rendered in the flight map view but not in the Tracking Station. The log proved the renderer fully executed in the TS (scene=TRACKSTATION frames with drawn=1 for ~20s during the launch leg, builds firing for every Mun member), so it was not a logic/gate problem but a VISIBILITY one. `GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.Driver.LateUpdate` set the per-leg VectorLine layer to `MapView.Draw3DLines ? 24 : 31`; layer 24 is the map-NODE/icon layer (`MapNode.Create(..., 24, ...)`), which the flight map camera renders but the TS map camera does not. KSP's own orbit lines (also Vectrosity, and confirmed visible in BOTH scenes) keep `OrbitRendererBase.layerMask = 31` unconditionally and put every orbit VectorLine on it (decompiled `OrbitRendererBase`: `protected int layerMask = 31;` + `l.rectTransform.gameObject.layer = layerMask;`), regardless of `Draw3DLines`. **Fix:** `const int targetLayer = 31;` always (the polyline always uses `Draw3D()`, so it belongs on the same 3D orbit-line layer stock uses). One-line change; no new pure logic, so verified by the TS playtest. Ruled out (with evidence) two wrong theories first: the cache is NOT left holding scene-destroyed VectorLines (`onGameStateLoad -> Clear()` fires on every scene change, e.g. 00:29:00 entering the TS, so TS lines are freshly built valid GameObjects), and it is NOT warp-flash brevity (the launch leg drew for ~20 continuous seconds and was still invisible).
- **Ghost trajectory polyline jittered under time warp in the Tracking Station (playtest 2026-05-30, `logs/2026-05-30_0056_ts-polyline-jitter`, fixed):** once visible in the TS, the polyline oscillated between two almost-overlapping positions; the user confirmed it is steady at 1x and the gap between the two positions grows with the warp multiplier. That signature = the surface positions were being resolved through a body state that desyncs from the render frame by ~one warp step. The renderer called `CelestialBody.GetWorldSurfacePosition(lat,lon,alt)` for every point EVERY frame; decompiled, that is `BodyFrame.LocalToWorld(GetRelSurfacePosition(...).xzy).xzy + position`, and `BodyFrame` updates on the physics/warp cadence, so consecutive render frames sampled orientations a warp-step apart and alternated between them. Stock orbit lines do not jitter because they are inertial (Keplerian, no body rotation): decompiled `OrbitRendererBase` computes points via `ScaledSpace.LocalToScaledSpace(orbitPoints)` with a zeroed `rectTransform` (line 465/532) exactly like the polyline, so the shared absolute-scaled + zeroed-transform pattern was confirmed NOT the cause; the body CENTRE (`position`) is stable too (stock lines use it and do not jitter). The only jittering term was the body ORIENTATION. **Fix (`GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.Driver`):** capture each leg point ONCE in the render-stable scaled planet's LOCAL frame (`body.scaledBody.transform.InverseTransformPoint(LocalToScaledSpace(GetWorldSurfacePosition(...)))`) and re-project it through `scaledBody.transform.TransformPoint(...)` every frame. The scaled planet rotates smoothly per render frame (continents do not jitter in the map), so the polyline follows the body's spin without resampling `BodyFrame`. The capture is refreshed whenever `TimeWarp.CurrentRate <= 1x` (where `TransformPoint(InverseTransformPoint(x)) == x`, identical to the old direct path and free of any BodyFrame-vs-scaledBody discrepancy) and FROZEN under warp; new `LegPolyline.localScaled` field holds the captured locals, reset to null on cache rebuild (scene change) so it recaptures against the new scene's scaled body. Falls back to the old direct per-frame path only when `scaledBody` is unavailable. Unity-rendering change (no new pure logic); verified by the TS playtest. Diagnosed by confirming with the user that it is warp-coupled (steady at 1x) before touching the geometry path.
- **Tracking Station loop-member handoff blackout (~1-5s gap between legs) (playtest 2026-05-30, `logs/2026-05-30_0134_ts-handoff-gap`, fixed):** at each member-to-member handoff in a looped mission, the previous leg's orbit line + ghost disappeared and the next appeared only ~1s (sometimes longer) later. Confirmed from the log: at the Mun-phase handoff the markers swept #16/#13/#14/#17 around 01:30:41-43, then NOTHING (proto tracked=0, polyline drawn=0, no atmospheric marker) until #18's first marker at 01:30:48.8 (~5.5s). Root cause: the TS create/remove pass (`GhostMapPresence.UpdateTrackingStationGhostLifecycle`, driven from `ParsekTrackingStation.Update`) is throttled to `LifecycleCheckIntervalSec = 2.0s`, so the incoming member's proto-vessel orbit line could not be created until up to ~2s after the outgoing member's was removed; during a member's ORBITAL phase the orbit line is the ONLY thing on screen (the polyline correctly stays off and there is no atmospheric marker), so the lag reads as a full blackout. The polyline (per-frame, not lifecycle-throttled) was NOT the gap; its `drawn=0` during that window is correct (orbital phase). **Fix:** lowered the single `LifecycleCheckIntervalSec` from `2.0f` to `0.25f` for ALL Tracking Station ghost rendering (not just loops), so handoffs are prompt and ordinary recordings also refresh promptly. (First cut gated a short cadence behind "loop active"; simplified per user request to one fast cadence everywhere, since the per-tick cost is light regardless.) A no-mutation tick only re-scans sources and reseeds a few already-tracked ghost orbits; the expensive create/destroy + stock vessel-list rebuild fire only at actual boundaries regardless of cadence, so running 4x/s instead of 0.5x/s just removes the lag. Flight scene was already prompt (its create path is the per-frame `CheckPendingMapVessels` pending queue, not a throttled lifecycle), so only the TS path needed it. No new pure logic; verified by the TS playtest.
- **Deferred item C (pre-merge Opus review SHOULD-FIX, tracked not fixed): the TS CREATE path's EndpointTail override is not loop-member-gated, unlike the refresh path + flight scene.** The refresh path now suppresses the endpoint tail for loop members (`EndpointTailAllowedInTrackingStationUpdate`), and the flight gap fallback (`ParsekPlaybackPolicy.TryResolveTerminalFallbackMapOrbitUpdate`) rejects `EndpointTail` (accepts only `TerminalOrbit`) and applies the loop shift. But the shared TS create path (`ResolveTrackingStationGhostSourceCore` -> `ResolveTrackingStationGhostSource` with `allowTerminalOrbitFallback=true`, then `CreateGhostVesselFromSource`) can still resolve `EndpointTail` and seeds it with NO loop epoch shift - the same 181 Mm class. Verified INERT for the real Mun mission: the transfer gap has continuous recorded track coverage, so the create path returns `before-terminal-orbit`/None mid-gap and never recreates a loop ghost there. The narrow residual risk is a loop member in a SPARSE orbit gap (no recorded coverage between two orbit segments -> `allowSparseOrbitGapFallback` true) whose terminal is endpoint-segment-family: it could be re-seeded via the create EndpointTail at an unshifted historical position for a frame, then flicker. Proper fix: thread a loop-member flag (or the epoch shift) into `ResolveMapPresenceGhostSource` / `ResolveTrackingStationGhostSourceCore` / `CreateGhostVesselFromSource` and suppress the `EndpointTail` source for loop members, mirroring the refresh-path gate. Not fixed pre-merge because the resolver is shared with the flight scene (broadens risk) and the case is inert for real recordings; the reviewer's verdict was "acceptable to merge as-is, track the asymmetry." Full review found NO blockers. **Update (2026-05-28):** the zero-drift PR's create-time loop-shift fix (commit `77a368a3`) partially mitigates this — `CreateGhostVesselFromSource` now accepts `loopEpochShiftSeconds`, threads it into the EndpointTail branch, and the lifecycle create caller (`UpdateTrackingStationGhostLifecycle`) passes `tsLoopEpochShift`. So the lifecycle path NO LONGER seeds an unshifted EndpointTail for a loop member. The residual risk now lives only on the TS STARTUP create path (`CreateGhostVesselsFromCommittedRecordings` at `ParsekTrackingStation.cs:185` / `Patches/GhostTrackingStationPatch.cs:446`), which still passes shift=0 because it has no `effUT` / `loopUnits` plumbing. That residual is the same scope as the sibling TODO immediately above (the ~313ms wrong-position icon flash at TS entry); fixing them together is the cleanest path.
- **Removed the "Show ghosts in Tracking Station" setting (done):** the toggle and its entire support machinery were removed; Parsek ghosts now ALWAYS appear in the Tracking Station (vessel list + map view), as if the setting were permanently on. Deleted the `ParsekSettings.showGhostsInTrackingStation` field and all of its persistence in `ParsekSettingsPersistence.cs` (key/store field/load/reconcile/`RecordShowGhostsInTrackingStation`/`EffectiveShowGhostsInTrackingStation`/save/reset/test accessors). Removed the two runtime gates in `GhostMapPresence.cs` (`UpdateTrackingStationGhostLifecycle` early-return and `CreateGhostVesselsFromCommittedRecordings` skip) so both run unconditionally, and the flip-detection + `lastKnownShowGhosts` field + `HideTrackingStationGhostsNow` + atmospheric-marker gate (and dead `HiddenBySetting` summary counter) in `ParsekTrackingStation.cs`. Dropped the UI toggle + reset in `UI/SettingsWindowUI.cs` and the `ShowGhostsInTrackingStation` field/initializer in `UI/SettingsWindowPresentation.cs`. Tests: deleted `ShowGhostsInTrackingStationTests.cs`, the #388 flip in-game test `ShowGhostsInTrackingStation_FlipRemovesAndRecreates`, and the off-disable TS test `CreateGhostVesselsFromCommittedRecordings_ShowGhostsDisabled_SkipsGhostCreation`; pruned the now-no-op precondition lines in `GhostMapPresenceTests.cs`, `TrackingStationSpawnTests.cs`, `SettingsWindowPresentationTests.cs`, and `RuntimeTests.cs`.
- **Post-#958 full Opus review follow-ups (done on `design-mission-periodicity` after #958 merged):** (S1) `MissionsWindowUI.MissionSpanSeconds` (period-cell effective-cadence display) and `ResolveMissionWatchTarget` (Watch button) keyed off the legacy `ExcludedThroughLineHeadIds`, which the current UI never writes, so they ignored interval-level trims the loop builder applies via `ExcludedIntervalKeys` (period showed the untrimmed span; watch could consider trimmed-out vessels, though the runtime `HasActiveGhost` guard kept it from actually targeting a non-rendered ghost). Fixed by extracting the builder's member+window computation into `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.ComputeTrimmedMemberWindows` (single source of truth) and routing both UI helpers + `TryBuildMissionUnit` through it; new `MissionLoopUnitBuilderTests.ComputeTrimmedMemberWindows_HonorsIntervalTrim_SharedByBuilderAndUI`. Nits: (N1) removed the dead `firstActive`/`maxInstances` block + unused param from `GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputeNewestMissionInstanceSpanLoopUT` (the overlap cap never clamps the newest cycle; updated the one engine caller + 3 tests); (N3) corrected the `ParsekFlight.DriveMissionLoopUnits` signature comment (folds both head ids + interval keys + anchor + tree topology, not just head ids); (N4) `ParsekKSC.LogUnitTransitionKscIfChanged` now scans the TRIMMED member window (matching the flight engine) instead of raw recorded bounds. Full suite green (12590).
- **Non-protovessel ghost map marker: sticky label pin moved to right-click, menu stays on left-click, icon tint matched to the stock ProtoVessel icon (issue 2026-05-27, fixed):** the manually-drawn ghost markers (`MapMarkerRenderer`, the ones with a yellow "Ghost:" label, shown for ghosts that have no map ProtoVessel) pinned their sticky label on LEFT-click, which collided with the left-click menu (in the Tracking Station, opening the ghost popup) and was inconsistent with how the ProtoVessel icons keep their label. Decoupled the two interactions by button: `MapMarkerRenderer.IsToggleClick` now matches the RIGHT button (Unity button 1) so right-click pins/unpins the yellow label in both flight map view and the Tracking Station (mirroring the ProtoVessel icons), and a new `IsHandlerClick` (LEFT button 0) gates `ShouldRouteMarkerClickToHandler`, so a LEFT-click still opens the marker's `onClick` menu (the TS ghost popup) and otherwise passes through to the stock map / TS handlers. Renamed the `onLeftClick` handler param to `onClick` and updated the class/inline comments. For the icon look, the goal was to MATCH the stock ProtoVessel map icon the same ghost shows once it reaches orbit, not pick an arbitrary alpha. Decompiled `OrbitRenderer` / `OrbitRendererBase.objectNode_OnUpdateIcon` / `KSP.UI.Screens.Mapview.MapNode`: a vessel's `OrbitRenderer` ctor sets `nodeColor = (0.71,0.71,0.71,1)` and the object icon draws at `data.color = nodeColor.A(lineOpacity)` with `img.color = vData.color`; `lineOpacity == 1` for a visible in-front node (only fades to 0.5 behind a body via `MAPNODE_BEHINDBODY_OPACITY`). Both the marker and the ProtoVessel icon draw the SAME atlas sprite (indices matched in #387), so the atlas branch in `DrawMarkerAtScreen` now tints with the new `StockVesselIconColor = (0.71,0.71,0.71,1)` constant (not opacity-modulated by sticky/hover, matching stock) instead of `WithMarkerOpacity(Color.white, sticky)`. `UnpinnedMarkerAlpha` stays 0.8 (it still drives the yellow hover/pin LABEL and the fallback diamond, both unchanged), so the `WithMarkerOpacity` unit test and the `MapMarkerOpacityMatchesPinnedState` in-game canary remain at 0.8. Updated the click-contract unit tests (`IsToggleClick` now right-only, new `IsHandlerClick` left-only, `ShouldRouteMarkerClickToHandler` left-click contract, `Format*ClickLogLine` button ids) and added `StockVesselIconColor_MatchesStockUnfocusedVesselNodeColor`.
- **TS ghost marker menu vanished unless the mouse button was held (issue 2026-05-27, fixed):** diagnosed from `logs/2026-05-27_2216_ghost-icon-leftclick-menu`: clicking a Tracking Station atmospheric ghost marker selected it (`button=0`) and opened the ghost popup, which was then dismissed `reason=outside-click` on the next MouseUp - the release of the very click that opened it. The popup anchors just below the cursor (`PositionPopupAtCursor` with a `Vector2.down` offset), so the cursor sits at/above the popup's top edge (outside its rect), and `CheckGhostPopupOutsideClick` dismissed on any outside MouseUp once past a 5-frame arm window; holding the button kept it open because no MouseUp fired. Fix: dismiss on a fresh outside PRESS (`Input.GetMouseButtonDown`) instead of a release, via the new pure predicate `ParsekTrackingStation.ShouldDismissGhostPopupOnOutsideClick(framesSinceOpen, freshClickThisFrame, mouseOverPopup)` (arm window + fresh press + cursor outside popup), so neither the press nor the release of the opening click can close the menu it just opened. This is independent of the right-click change above: the menu still opens on LEFT-click, and the original hypothesis that the button move alone would fix it does not hold (the dismiss watched both buttons, so the opening click's release closed it regardless of which button opened it). 5 new predicate cases in `TrackingStationControlSurfaceUITests`; the Unity Input polling itself is playtest-validated. Full suite green (12594).
