## TODO - Missions: looped inter-body launch-window phase-lock (DEFERRED to a new PR after #958)

- **Known limitation shipped in #958 (playtest 2026-05-26, evidence `logs/2026-05-26_2329_mun-mission-map-desync`):** a looped mission that crosses bodies (the Mun-landing "Kerbal X" tree) does not phase-align its replay to the live sky. Member #15 replays its recorded Kerbin transfer ellipse (`sma=6,274,896 ecc=0.873 peri=799 km`) then a recorded Mun approach hyperbola (`sma=-720,778 ecc=1.380 peri=273 km`) with a Kerbin->Mun SOI handoff baked into the recording, but the loop runs at an arbitrary `phaseAnchor` (54042.92 / 5861.38) unrelated to the recorded launch UT (`span start = 3991.76`), and there is ZERO launch-window / re-aim / phase-align logic (grep count 0). The recorded elements are in Kerbin's inertial frame at a fixed orientation and the Mun arc is Mun-relative, so at an arbitrary live UT: (1) Kerbin has rotated, so the orbit periapsis (recorded inertial orientation, once over KSC) no longer sits over the live launch site; (2) the Mun is at a different orbital phase, so the transfer apoapsis points at empty space and the Mun-relative landing arc renders at the Mun's CURRENT location, disconnected from the Kerbin transfer arc. INHERENT to replaying a celestial-phase-dependent trajectory at the wrong time - NOT a regression and NOT caused by the map-presence epoch-shift fix (that only places the ghost at the right phase ALONG its recorded ellipse; it cannot move the live Mun or re-orient the recorded inertial ellipse).
- **Goal:** determine the correct launch UT(s) so the looped replay's map / Tracking Station trajectories line up with the recorded geometry. Faithful launches happen at `UT0 + k*P` (UT0 = recorded launch = span start), where P is the period at which the bodies the mission depends on return to their recorded-launch configuration.
- **Decomposition of P:** (a) launch-body rotation phase (`body.rotationPeriod`, Kerbin sidereal day ~21,549 s) realigns the orbit over the launch site; (b) each transited body's orbital phase (`transitBody.orbit.period`, Mun ~138,984 s) realigns the intercept. Single-body missions: `P = rotation period` (clean, frequent, fully faithful). Inter-body: joint best-fit of (a)+(b) - the periods are incommensurate so it repeats only approximately, at a multiple of the dominant (intercept) period; this is also the physically-real launch-window cadence, which naturally bounds the instance count.
- **Proposed two tiers:** Tier 1 - phase-lock the loop to the dominant intercept period (target body's orbital period), aligned to `UT0`, so the transfer actually reaches the target (fixes the big visual break); quantize the loop cadence to multiples of P and align the phase anchor to `UT0 mod P`. Tier 2 - joint rotation+orbital best-fit so the orbit also sits over the launch site, plus multi-transfer chains (Kerbin->Mun->Minmus, interplanetary).
- **Open decisions (pick before building):** faithful-only mode (cadence always snapped to the launch-window period) vs a per-mission "faithful / free (decorative)" toggle; and for inter-body, accept approximately-faithful (small residual phase error, usable) vs exact-only (rare, very long period). Needs a short design note for the multi-body best-fit math + how to surface a quantized/long cadence in the Missions UI.
- **Relationship to the instance-count question:** the earlier "20 ghosts per render distance instead of per whole mission span" idea is PARKED behind this - faithful inter-body cadence is naturally long (one launch per window), so the instance count stays small without changing the cap. Revisit the render-distance cap (max self-proximity dwell within ~50 km / `LoopSimplifiedMeters`, vs `span/20` in `GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputeEffectiveLaunchCadence`) only after the phase-lock lands, and only if frequent same-body looping still needs it.
- **Phase 0 (done):** pure constraint extraction. New `Source/Parsek/MissionPeriodicity.cs` (`IBodyInfo` seam + `FlightGlobalsBodyInfo` impl, `ConstraintKind` / `PhaseConstraint` / `Support` / `ConstraintExtraction` types, and `internal static ExtractConstraints`). It reads the trimmed member set (`MissionLoopUnitBuilder.ComputeTrimmedMemberWindows`), classifies each included segment (surface/atmospheric `TrackSection` -> `Rotation(B)`; `bodyName` change across `OrbitSegments` / OrbitalCheckpoint checkpoints -> `Orbital(C)`; bare inertial orbit -> nothing), and flags `UnsupportedCrossParent` (sibling target like Duna) / `UnsupportedRendezvous` (Relative-to-vessel section). No wiring yet (nothing calls it), so zero behavior change. 15 pure tests in `MissionPeriodicityTests.cs` cover every Test-Plan case (single-body orbit -> empty; launch+orbit -> one Rotation; Mun mission -> Rotation+Orbital direct-child; cross-parent Duna -> UnsupportedCrossParent; transient flyby -> Orbital present; checkpoint-bridged backgrounded SOI still surfaces the body change; predicted tail / zero-rotation / retrograde guards; tidal-lock collapse).
- **Q3 over-constraint fix (done):** `ExtractConstraints` previously emitted `Rotation(B)` for ANY included surface/atmospheric segment of B. That over-constrained a config with no inertial orbit of B to hand off to: a pure surface/atmospheric arc is recorded surface-relative and renders at its correct ground location at ANY universe time (it rotates with B), so it imposes NO phase constraint (the design's "no-inertial-arc -> MinCycleDuration" edge case). Fix: `Rotation(B)` is now emitted ONLY when the included set has BOTH a surface/atmospheric segment of B AND an inertial-orbit segment of B (the ascent->orbit / orbit->descent hand-off) - the rotation phase only matters to line a surface segment's hand-off up to an inertial orbit of the same body. The launch body's own orbit segments stay in `earliestOrbitStartByBody` (rule 4 only skips them as SOI ENTRIES), so the hand-off check sees them. Preserved: "launch + Kerbin orbit" still yields `Rotation(Kerbin)`; "atmospheric ascent only" -> empty set -> `P = MinCycleDuration` (free loop); the Mun mission unchanged. Updated design-doc "What determines P" rules 1/2 + the phases-plan vocabulary to say the constraint requires the hand-off (not a bare surface arc). 2 new tests (`Extract_AtmosphericOnly_NoOrbit_NoRotationConstraint` end-to-end through Solve -> MinCycleDuration; `Extract_LaunchPlusOrbit_StillLocksRotation_HandoffRegressionGuard`); updated the retrograde + zero-rotation tests to include the hand-off so they exercise their intended guard.
- **Phase 3 UI (done, built on the Phase-1 Tier-1 solution; NOT Phase 2):** the Missions tab now surfaces the periodicity per looping mission (`MissionsWindowUI`). It computes the solution once per mission per frame in `ComputeMissionPeriodicity` (`ExtractConstraints` + `Solve` over the per-frame cached `view`/`compRoots`, `RecordingStore.CommittedRecordings`, the mission's `ExcludedIntervalKeys`, `FlightGlobalsBodyInfo.Instance`, and `referenceUT = Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()` for the live countdown), suppressing the per-call Verbose lines and emitting one `VerboseRateLimited` summary instead. New "Time to launch" header column placed right after "Missions and vessels" (the name column), before "Start time" (`ColW_TMinus = 90`, folded into `MissionHeaderRightBlockWidth`). The live countdown sits on the mission's launch (first) vessel row, under that column header, via `DrawTMinusVesselCell` (every other vessel row + the mission header bar leave a same-width blank cell so the data columns stay aligned); the draw loop computes the periodicity once per mission and passes it to both the header period cell and the launch-row cell. The cell shows the four states via the pure `BuildTMinusCellText`: blank (not looping) / "not aligned" (unsupported no-lock sentinel: cross-parent / rendezvous) / "continuous" (`P == MinCycleDuration`) / "T- <countdown>" (supported), tinted amber when the locked window misses tolerance, and is drawn un-dimmed even when the launch interval is excluded (mission-level data, not a property of that interval). The period cell shows the faithful P + basis label ("~6h (Kerbin rot)" / "~1.6d (Mun window)") as a read-only tinted cell when phase-locked + constrained (via `BuildPeriodCellDisplay` + the dominant constraint from `SelectDominantConstraintIndex`), widened to `ColW_PeriodLocked = ColW_Period + ColW_TMinus + 4` (reclaiming the width freed by moving the countdown off the bar) so "~P (basis)" fits on one line; otherwise the existing editable cadence cell. Pure helpers (`FormatCountdownCompact`, `FormatPeriodCompact`, `BuildPeriodBasisLabel`, `BuildPeriodCellDisplay`, `BuildTMinusCellText`, `ComputeNextRelaunchUT`) are unit-tested (28 tests in `MissionsWindowPeriodicityDisplayTests`, incl. zero/negative/NaN + the four states + Kerbin/Earth day length + the relaunch-schedule cases below); the IMGUI layout is playtest-verified. `MissionsWindowUI.cs` is already on the ERS/ELS allowlist. Phase 2 (joint best-fit) + Phase 4 (synodic) stay deferred; the UI only DISPLAYS the Phase-1 solution.
  - **Flight-map custom-icon loop-clock fix (done):** the flight-scene custom map marker (`ParsekUI.DrawMapMarkers` -> `TryComputeGhostWorldPosition`) sampled the ghost trajectory at the LIVE `Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()`. For a looped-mission member whose mesh is hidden by zone distance (the launch / atmospheric phase, which has no orbit -> no map ProtoVessel), the recorded points sit at the original (past) UTs, so the live UT is always `OutsideTimeRange` -> `positionFailure` -> the icon never draws (KSP.log showed `candidates>=1 drawn=0 positionFailure=1 missingBody=0` every frame in map view, while the proto-vessel orbit ghosts rendered fine). #958 threaded the span-clock into the proto-vessel path but missed this custom-marker path. Fix: before computing the position, map the live UT to the shared span-clock effUT via `GhostPlaybackLogic.ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT(idx, rec.StartUT, rec.EndUT, liveUT, flight.Engine.CurrentLoopUnits, out loopHidden)` (the SAME scene-agnostic resolver the TS / proto-vessel paths use; identity for a non-loop ghost or an Empty unit set, so non-loop behavior is byte-identical) and skip the frame when `loopHidden` (the shared clock has the member outside its window, matching the engine's mesh-hide decision). Surface-relative lat/lon/alt at the live body rotation puts the icon at the correct rotating ground position. New `MapMarkerSummary.LoopHidden` counter distinguishes a loop-clock skip from a position failure; 2 tests (`MapMarkerSummary_IncludesPrioritySkipCounters` extended + `MapMarkerSummary_LoopHiddenAloneHasSignal`). The position mapping reuses the already-tested `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT`; in-game-verified.
  - **T- relaunch-cadence fix (done):** the T- countdown originally targeted `solution.NextWindowUT` = the next faithful P-window from now (`UT0 + k*P >= now`). But the loop engine does NOT relaunch at every P-window: `TryBuildMissionUnit` quantizes the cadence to `effectiveOverlapCadence = QuantizeCadenceToMultipleOfP(overlapCadence, P) = m*P` (m can be >= 2 when the recording span or the user period exceeds P), so it relaunches only every m-th window and SKIPS the rest. The old countdown ticked to "T- 0s" on a window with no launch. Fix: `MissionsWindowUI` now rebuilds the REAL `LoopUnitSet` once per frame (cached by `Time.frameCount` in `GetLoopUnitSet`, mirroring `GetMissionView`/`GetCompositionRoots`) via `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build(MissionStore.Missions, CommittedTrees, CommittedRecordings, autoLoopIntervalSeconds, FlightGlobalsBodyInfo.Instance)` (the SAME inputs the scene drivers pass, so the same unit; Verbose summary suppressed), resolves the mission's unit (`TryResolveMissionUnit` maps the mission's trimmed members to committed indices and looks one up via `LoopUnitSet.TryGetUnitForMember`), and the new pure `internal static ComputeNextRelaunchUT(unit, now)` derives the next ACTUAL relaunch = `phaseAnchorUT + n * relaunchCadence` (relaunchCadence = `OverlapCadenceSeconds` when it overlaps the span, else `CadenceSeconds`; `n = max(0, ceil((now - phaseAnchorUT) / relaunchCadence))`). `MissionPeriodicityDisplay` surfaces `NextRelaunchUT` + `UnitBuilt`; `BuildTMinusCellText` takes the relaunch UT + a `unitBuilt` flag (a mission with no engine unit reads "not aligned") instead of `NextWindowUT`. Display-only: the UI's `LoopUnitSet` is never pushed to the engine, so `TryBuildMissionUnit`'s behavior is unchanged. 7 new tests (the `m=2` regression guard proving the countdown targets the 2P relaunch not the skipped P-window, overlap-vs-span cadence selection, parked-before-anchor clamp, exact-boundary no-skip, degenerate-cadence fallback, no-unit-built "not aligned").
- **Phase 1 (done):** single-constraint (Tier-1) phase-lock, wired into the loop builder (gated). New `MissionPeriodicity.Solve(constraints, support, ut0, nowUT, IBodyInfo)` -> `PeriodicitySolution` (P, NextWindowUT, ResidualSeconds, WithinTolerance, Support, ShouldPhaseLock, Method): unsupported -> no-lock sentinel; 0 constraints -> `P = MinCycleDuration`; one Rotation -> rotationPeriod; one direct-child Orbital -> `C.orbit.period`; tidally-locked Rotation+Orbital (equal periods) -> that period; the Mun case (Rotation(Kerbin)+Orbital(Mun), differing periods) -> lock the dominant `Orbital(Mun)` and KNOWINGLY drop+log the Kerbin-rotation residual; any other multi-independent set still locks the dominant intercept and logs the residual (the full joint best-fit is Phase 2). `NextWindowUT` = smallest `UT0 + k*P >= nowUT` (k may be negative for a future-dated UT0); guards `P <= 0` / NaN -> MinCycleDuration. Wired into `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.TryBuildMissionUnit` (new optional `IBodyInfo` arg, default null = no lock = today's behavior): a supported config snaps `phaseAnchorUT = NextWindowUT` (referenced to `LoopAnchorUT`, stable across frames) and quantizes the span + overlap cadence to a multiple of P (above the existing `MinCycleDuration` / overlap-cap floors via `QuantizeCadenceToMultipleOfP`); an unsupported / no-body-info config is byte-identical to the merged #958 looping. `BuildSignature` folds in the looping tree's transited-body set + their live periods (only when `IBodyInfo` is supplied) so a body-geometry change rebuilds. The three scene drivers (`ParsekFlight` / `ParsekTrackingStation` / `ParsekKSC`) pass `FlightGlobalsBodyInfo.Instance`. `Info`-on-build logs `PhaseLock APPLIED` (old->new anchor + window) / `PhaseLock SKIPPED` (unsupported reason); `Warn` when the Tier-1 residual exceeds tolerance. 21 new tests (solver Tier-1 cases + next-window k incl. future-dated UT0 + tidal collapse + over-constrained + tolerance boundary; builder snaps a supported single-body / same-parent config + leaves an unsupported one at the raw anchor + byte-identical no-body-info path; signature rebuild on body-geometry change; phase-lock applied/skipped/over-constrained log assertions). Affects ONLY looping Missions; cross-parent stays `UnsupportedCrossParent` (gated to today's behavior until Phase 4).
- **Phase 2 (done): joint best-fit over whole multiples of the dominant period.** Playtest showed the Tier-1 Mun loop locked the Mun intercept but dropped the Kerbin-rotation residual WHOLESALE (~9688s / ~161deg of launch-pad misalignment), so the launch did not line up with the pad. `MissionPeriodicity.Solve` now, for an incommensurate multi-constraint config, searches whole multiples `m` in `[1, MaxJointMultiples=16]` of the dominant constraint's period (so the dominant body stays locked at every relaunch) and picks the `m` that MINIMIZES the worst dropped-constraint circular phase error over one cadence step (`m*P`), preferring the smallest `m` on a tie (`JointResidualTieEpsilonSeconds`) so the relaunch period stays as short as the alignment allows. New pure helpers `FindBestJointMultiple` + `JointStepResidual` (both `internal static`, unit-tested). `P = m*dominantPeriod`; `ResidualSeconds` = the per-cycle drift at `m` (the fixed cadence still drifts on incommensurate periods - see the zero-drift task below); `WithinTolerance` compares it to the physics tolerance; `Method = "joint-best-fit"` when `m>1`, else `"dominant-intercept"`. For the stock Kerbin-rotation (21549.425s) + Mun-orbit (138984.38s) case the best multiple is `m=9` (~14.5 days): pad residual `9688s/161deg -> ~993s/16deg` (~10x better; still amber, a fixed cadence can't hit the quarter-degree tolerance). Single-constraint + tidal-lock configs are unchanged (`m=1`, residual 0). 3 broken Tier-1 tests updated (Mun case, over-constrained two-rotations, builder same-parent snap) + 3 new (`FindBestJointMultiple` exact-resonance / stays-at-one, `JointStepResidual` worst-dropped). `MaxJointMultiples` is a documented, easy-to-tune constant.
- **Phase 2.5: zero-drift per-window reschedule (IN PROGRESS; the accurate-for-supply-routes follow-up).** The current best-fit uses a FIXED cadence (`m*dominantPeriod`), which cannot hold incommensurate periods aligned forever: each successive relaunch's dropped-constraint (launch-pad) error grows by the per-cycle residual (e.g. ~993s/cycle for the Mun case). For supply-route-grade accuracy the loop instead re-solves each relaunch INDEPENDENTLY to the true next joint near-coincidence after the previous launch, so the pad error stays BOUNDED (~one residual) instead of accumulating. Plan: `docs/dev/plans/zero-drift-reschedule.md` (math, schedule representation, gating, phasing). Key insight (plan §2.1): the per-constraint phase offsets cancel, so a launch `L = UT0 + k*dominantPeriod` satisfies constraint i iff `CircularPhaseError(k*dominantPeriod, period_i) <= tol_i` - an ABSOLUTE function of k, so picking good k never accumulates. Only multi-constraint incommensurate ("drifting") configs get a schedule; single/tidal/unconstrained/unsupported keep the existing fixed cadence (byte-identical). Scheduled units are gated non-overlapping so the overlap engine path is untouched.
  - **Phase A (done): pure solver.** New in `MissionPeriodicity.cs`: `NextJointNearCoincidenceUT` / `TryFindNextScheduleK` (lock the dominant exactly; smallest within-tolerance k in `ScheduleLookaheadMultiples=4096`, else bounded-best min-residual k - never accumulating), `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule` (gates on >=2 distinct-period constraints; filters degenerate dropped periods with a Warn; returns null for single/tidal/unsupported), and the immutable `MissionRelaunchSchedule` class (snapshotted inputs + lazily-extended launch-UT cache + `TryResolveActiveLaunch` / `NextLaunchAfter` + `MinIntervalSeconds` for the overlap gate + `MaxScheduleSteps=8192` CPU safety cap). `GhostPlaybackLogic.LoopUnit` gains a nullable `RelaunchSchedule` field + a null-chaining constructor overload (no consumers yet, byte-identical for every existing config). 22 pure tests in `MissionZeroDriftScheduleTests.cs` (the hand-checkable synthetic 100/31 case incl. the non-uniform within-tol sequence 9/13/18/22 and intervals 400/500/400; the stock Mun case proving non-accumulation vs fixed cadence; tolerance boundary; multi-dropped worst=max; bounded-best fallback; degenerate/NaN/floor/future-dated guards; the safety cap parks + Warns + `NextLaunchAfter` NaN; monotonic resolution). No behavior change in game (nothing attaches a schedule until Phase B wires the builder). Math core reviewed clean-context.
  - **Phase B (done): builder wiring + span-clock consumption.** `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.TryBuildMissionUnit` now, for a phase-locked DRIFTING config (>=2 distinct-period constraints, the Mun/Minmus case), calls `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule` and, when the schedule is non-overlapping (`MinIntervalSeconds >= span`, the INVARIANT keeping the overlap engine path off scheduled units), attaches it to the `LoopUnit`: `phaseAnchorUT = schedule.FirstLaunchUT` (a within-tolerance window >= the first-play floor) and `CadenceSeconds = OverlapCadenceSeconds = max(span, MinIntervalSeconds)`. A would-overlap schedule is rejected (fixed cadence kept, logged `zeroDrift=rejected-would-overlap`). Single/tidal/unconstrained/unsupported configs get no schedule and are byte-identical to the prior fixed cadence. `GhostPlaybackLogic.TryComputeSpanLoopUT` + `DecideUnitMemberRender` take an optional `MissionRelaunchSchedule` (null = the existing uniform path, byte-identical): when present they resolve the active launch from the schedule (largest scheduled launch <= currentUT), measure the in-span phase from it, and park in the inter-cycle tail between launches (render nothing). Threaded through all consumers: the flight engine single-instance branch + the loop-synced-debris parent-span branch (passes `parentUnit.RelaunchSchedule` so debris rides its scheduled parent), `ParsekKSC`, and `ParsekTrackingStation` via `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT` (+ the flight-map custom marker / `GhostMapPresence` through the same resolver). The Mun config is now scheduled (the prior fixed m=9 ~14.5d cadence is gone for it); the two Phase-2 builder tests that encoded that contract were updated. Review fixes folded in: (a) the loop-synced-debris parent-span branch now CONSUMES `isInInterCycleTail` (routes it through `parentPaused`) so ride-along debris whose end is at/after the parent span end is hidden in the inter-launch gap instead of rendering a frozen stale ghost at the clamped spanEnd (a latent bug for any unit with `CadenceSeconds > span`, now reachable on every scheduled gap); (b) `BuildSignature`/`AppendTransitedBodyDigest` now folds `SoiRadius` + `OrbitalVelocity` (which feed the orbital tolerance, hence the within-tolerance windows) so a planet-pack SOI change re-derives the schedule; (c) `MinIntervalProbeLaunches` bumped to 8 (the non-overlap invariant itself is unconditional: `OverlapCadenceSeconds = max(span, MinInterval) >= span` regardless). New tests: builder attaches a schedule for the Mun config + non-overlap invariant, no schedule for single-constraint, would-overlap rejection; scheduled span-clock parked/render/tail + null-schedule byte-identical (incl. the reordered span<=0 guard) + `DecideUnitMemberRender` decisions + the `UnitMemberOverlaps==false` invariant; plus an in-game test (`TrackingStationSpanClock_ZeroDriftSchedule_ResolvesScheduledLaunch`) exercising the scheduled span clock through the live TS/map seam. The loop-synced-debris-rides-scheduled-parent path (engine:1820) is covered by the pure tail-flag test (`SpanClock_Scheduled_...ParksInTailBetweenLaunches`) plus the existing, in-game-verified `parentPaused` hide machinery the fix routes through (no dedicated in-game debris scenario, which would need a contrived live recording + the private debris path; the wiring + the tail flag it depends on are both verified). Full suite green (12697). Integration reviewed clean-context.
  - **Phase C + D (done): UI + hardening.** `MissionsWindowUI.ComputeNextRelaunchUT` now branches on `unit.RelaunchSchedule`: a scheduled unit's TTL countdown + "Warp to..." target both resolve to `schedule.NextLaunchAfter(now)` (the next NON-UNIFORM scheduled launch), not `phaseAnchor + n*cadence`. The Missions period cell shows a "varies" label for a scheduled (non-uniform) unit via the new pure `BuildScheduledPeriodCellDisplay` (e.g. "~3d (Mun window, varies)" at the max cadence, longer when the player throttles) off the schedule's `MinIntervalSeconds`, instead of the stale fixed `Solution.P`. The three scene drivers (flight/KSC/TS) were already correct after Phase B (they share the schedule-aware `DecideUnitMemberRender` / `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT`). Hardening: caching is signature-based for the scene drivers (the schedule object persists + lazily extends across frames; the signature folds the body geometry incl. SOI/velocity) and per-frame for the UI display mirror (acceptable: each search breaks early at the first within-tol k); persistence is structural (nothing new serialized, the schedule re-derives from the already-persisted inputs); overlap is invariant-gated. New tests: scheduled `ComputeNextRelaunchUT` targets the next scheduled launch, `BuildScheduledPeriodCellDisplay` "varies" strings, and a determinism guard (two independently-built schedules resolve identically, underpinning both "UI cannot diverge from playback" and "re-derives identically after reload"). Full suite green (12700).
  - **Model revision (anchor on the tightest constraint + player throttle; done):** the first cut anchored on the DOMINANT = longest-period constraint (the Mun) and required the rest within tolerance, which pinned the body with the GENEROUS (SOI-width) tolerance to zero error while demanding the TIGHT one (the pad) line up too: for the stock Mun the first faithful window was ~803 Mun periods (~3.5 years) - unusable. The s15 Mun-mission segment review (frame boundaries: the Mun-relative approach/landing block self-anchors to the live Mun, so the Mun only needs to be within its SOI-width tolerance at the SOI seam, NOT pixel-exact) showed the Mun should not be pinned. Reworked: `SelectAnchorConstraintIndex` now picks the constraint with the SMALLEST duty cycle (tolerance/period) - the launch-pad rotation, not the Mun - and `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule` anchors on it (`SelectDominantConstraintIndex` stays only for the fixed-cadence `Solve` fallback). This MAXIMIZES window frequency (rate ~ anchorPeriod / product(other duty cycles), so you pin the tightest to keep it out of the product): the stock Mun max cadence drops from ~3.5 years to ~3.25 Earth days (first faithful pad-anchored window j=13), and the launch lands PIXEL-PERFECT over the pad with the Mun within ~0.5 SOI. Added a player THROTTLE (`minSpacing`, the builder passes the requested relaunch period; Auto = every faithful window = max cadence; an explicit period skips faithful windows to launch less often) so the player picks a lower cadence for supply routes. `MissionRelaunchSchedule` renamed `dominantPeriod`->`anchorPeriod` / `dropped*`->`other*`, added the `minSpacing` throttle in `ExtendOnce`. Updated the two Mun builder tests (pad anchored exactly, Mun within SOI tol, ~13-pad-rotation first window) + new tests (`SelectAnchorConstraintIndex` picks the pad; throttle skips windows; max-cadence no-throttle). Plan + CHANGELOG updated (windows now recur every few days, not rare). Full suite green (12703). Future option (not implemented): re-chain the Mun-relative block to the actual SOI crossing to erase the boundary seam and loosen the Mun tolerance further - a playback-engine change.
  - **External-review follow-ups (done):** (S1) the overlap-reject gate previously trusted `MinIntervalSeconds` (only an 8-launch probe) and could wrongly pass if the true min gap occurred later. Fixed by FLOORING the throttle at the span (`minSpacing = cadence`, already `>= span`): the schedule places consecutive launches `>= minSpacing >= span` apart, so every interval is `>= span` and the unit is non-overlapping BY CONSTRUCTION, independent of the probe. The realistic faithful gap (days) is `>> span` so the floor only bites a pathological short-gap config (merging it to one-at-a-time playback); the defensive `MinIntervalSeconds >= span` gate is kept but now always passes (the would-overlap reject path is unreachable). `Build_DriftingButSpanExceedsInterval` retargeted to assert the schedule is attached + non-overlapping. (S2) `MissionRelaunchSchedule.NextLaunchAfter` (called every UI frame) was an O(cacheSize) linear scan; switched to a binary search like `TryResolveActiveLaunch`. (N1) corrected the `ScheduleLookaheadMultiples` comment to the anchor-on-pad model (k counts pad rotations; ~13 for launch+orbit-to-Mun, ~700 when a tidally-locked landing adds a tight Rotation(body) constraint). (N2) clarifying comment on `BuildScheduledPeriodCellDisplay` (the interval is pad-anchored; the basis label names the dominant celestial event the window targets). Full suite green (12703).
  - **Landing-body rotation A/B flag (done; was: stock s15 Mun period ~1.65 Kerbin years).** Cause confirmed from KSP.log: the s15 "Kerbal X" mission is a land-AND-return, so the extractor emits THREE constraints - `Rotation(Kerbin)` (pad, tol ~15s), `Orbital(Mun)` (intercept, SOI tol ~4480s), AND `Rotation(Mun)` (the Mun LANDING; tidally locked so period = Mun orbit, but carrying the tight 0.25deg launch-pad tolerance ~96s). Anchored on the pad, finding a window where the Mun ROTATION is also within 0.25deg is rare (`minInterval=15149245s`). The Mun landing is body-fixed (self-anchors to the Mun surface, like the KSC ascent), so it does not need the tight pad tolerance - its phase is already pinned within the SOI by `Orbital(Mun)`. Implemented BOTH options behind a player A/B flag (`ParsekSettings.transitedBodyRotationModeIndex` -> `TransitedBodyRotationMode` Drop/Loose/Tight; default **Loose**; Settings > Looping "Landing-body alignment" cycle button): **Drop** excludes a transited (non-launch) body's `Rotation(body)` constraint -> the SOI tolerance governs -> ~15 Kerbin days (largest handoff seam); **Loose** keeps it at `TransitedBodyLooseRotationDegrees=5deg` -> ~1-2 Kerbin months (small seam); **Tight** keeps the 0.25deg (~1.65 Kerbin years, pixel-perfect handoff). The launch-body (pad) rotation is NEVER dropped/loosened. `MissionPeriodicity.SelectAnchorConstraintIndex` / `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule` take `launchBodyName` + the mode (Drop pre-filters, Loose loosens via new `ScheduleToleranceSecondsFor`; new `IsTransitedBodyRotation` helper); `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build`/`TryBuildMissionUnit`/`BuildSignature` thread the mode (folded into the signature so a flipped flag rebuilds); the four scene/UI drivers pass `ParsekSettings.Current.TransitedBodyRotationMode`. Setting persists via stock GameParameters (public int field). New tests: the 3-mode first-window ordering (Drop<Loose<Tight), `ScheduleToleranceSecondsFor`/`IsTransitedBodyRotation`, and the Settings label/cycle helpers. Full suite green (12707).
  - **Separate (not a zero-drift regression): tracking-station 1-2s render delay.** Confirmed from KSP.log (TS: `destroy reason=gap-between-orbit-segments` at 00:33:44.860 -> next `create-dispatch` at 00:33:46.865 = ~2.0 real seconds). When a looped-mission replay crosses a GAP between two recorded orbit segments (here a ~62 game-second coast between the parking orbit [4181-4779] and the next orbit [4841-5727]), `GhostMapPresence` destroys the TS proto-vessel and recreates it at the next segment; at low warp the game-second gap is ~2 real seconds of nothing. Flight-map hides this via the custom span-clock marker that bridges the gap; the TS relies solely on the proto-vessel. Orthogonal to zero-drift (it depends on the recorded segment structure, not the launch schedule). **Subsumed (fix shared with the SOI/segment-flicker item below):** the same-body intra-block carry now keeps the TS proto-vessel alive across the gap too, so this 1-2s gap should be gone in practice. Confirm in the next TS playtest.
  - **SOI/segment flicker in flight map + TS (playtest 2026-05-28, `logs/2026-05-28_1826_soi-trajectory-flicker`, fixed):** approaching/inside Mun SOI the looped Mun-mission ghost's orbit line + icon flashed on/off across consecutive Mun-frame OrbitSegments (capture-burn, descent, return-burn transitions). Confirmed from KSP.log: pid=2775631560 cycled `reason=visible-segment lineActive=True` -> `reason=past-segment-end lineActive=False` -> `visible-segment` with new bounds every 1-3 real seconds for the whole Mun phase. Two coupled causes: (1) `ParsekPlaybackPolicy.CheckPendingMapVessels` (rate-limited 2a path) called `TrajectoryMath.FindOrbitSegmentForMapDisplay` which only carries across a gap when the surrounding segments are ORBIT-EQUIVALENT (same sma/ecc/inc/etc.); a brief Mun-frame intra-block gap between two DIFFERENT Mun orbits (capture burn) returned null -> destroyed the ProtoVessel + re-queued to pending -> recreated next tick. (2) `GhostOrbitLinePatch.Postfix` toggled `line.active=false` the moment currentUT walked past the current segment's endUT, before the segment selector picked the next segment (~one frame, ~300-500ms wall-clock at low warp), making the line blink even when the ghost survived. **Fix:** introduced same-body carry that intentionally does NOT require orbit equivalence. New pure helpers `TrajectoryMath.FindOrbitSegmentOrSameBodyCarry` (the previous segment carries across any same-body gap) and `TryGetBodyFrameBoundsForMapDisplay` (the bounds of the run of consecutive same-body segments around the playback head). `ParsekPlaybackPolicy.CheckPendingMapVessels` 2a + `GhostMapPresence.UpdateTrackingStationGhostLifecycle` (`coveringSegment` resolver) + `GetTrackingStationGhostRemovalReason` switched to the new carry, so the ghost is no longer torn down in same-body intra-block gaps. `UpdateGhostOrbitForRecording` now also caches body-frame bounds (loop-shifted by the same offset applied to `ghostOrbitBounds`) in a new `ghostBodyFrameOrbitBounds` dict; `TryGetBodyFrameOrbitBoundsForGhostVessel` reads it and `GhostOrbitLinePatch.Postfix` uses these wider bounds for the `line.active` decision while `GhostOrbitArcPatch` + `GhostOrbitIconClampPatch` keep using the per-segment bounds for arc clipping + icon clamping. New reasons: `visible-body-frame`, `past-body-frame-end`, `before-body-frame-start`. Result per the user spec: inside a body frame the orbit line stays continuously on (the arc shape itself still redraws per segment as the orbit driver retargets at each transition); only the actual SOI / body change blanks the line, and the ghost icon jumps from the end of its transfer arc to its correct-at-currentUT point in the destination-body trajectory. 9 new tests (active/gap-carry/body-change/past-last for `FindOrbitSegmentOrSameBodyCarry`, run-expansion/same-body-gap/body-change-gap/past-last/before-first for `TryGetBodyFrameBoundsForMapDisplay`). Full suite green (12716).
  - **Follow-up (playtest 2026-05-28, `logs/2026-05-28_1923_ts-rendering-after-alignment`, fixed): orbit-line blackout at TS entry + at flight-create for any loop-shifted ghost.** Confirmed from KSP.log: in TS, pid=3876519787 (Kerbal X #15) entered TS at 19:20:02.067 with `Cached body-frame bounds ... loopShift=0.00` (raw recorded UTs 4181-20094), `GhostOrbitLinePatch.Postfix` then fired `reason=past-body-frame-end lineActive=False bounds=[4181.1,20094.2] currentUT=35864231.1` (35M-second mismatch), and the cache refresh with the correct `loopShift=35858243.50` only landed at 19:20:04.071 — exactly the 2.0s `LifecycleCheckIntervalSec` later. Same shape in flight at 19:19:03 (~0.4s blackout, gated by the smaller `MapOrbitUpdateIntervalSec=0.5s`). Root cause: both `GhostMapPresence.CreateGhostVesselFromSource` callers (the TS lifecycle's CREATE pass and `ParsekPlaybackPolicy.CheckPendingMapVessels`'s deferred-create pass) computed the loop epoch shift and passed `effUT` for source-resolve / logging, but `CreateGhostVesselFromSource` -> `UpdateGhostOrbitForRecording` always ran with the default `loopEpochShiftSeconds = 0.0` — so the very first `ghostOrbitBounds` + `ghostBodyFrameOrbitBounds` entries held raw recorded UTs until the next rate-limited refresh re-applied them with the correct shift. **Fix:** threaded an optional `loopEpochShiftSeconds` parameter through both `CreateGhostVesselFromSource` overloads (default 0 for byte-identical non-loop behavior) into the Segment + EndpointTail dispatches, then updated the two loop-aware callers to pass it (`UpdateTrackingStationGhostLifecycle` passes `tsLoopEpochShift = currentUT - effUT`; `CheckPendingMapVessels` passes `pendingLoopEpochShift = currentUT - toCreate[i].effUT`). The startup path (`CreateGhostVesselsFromCommittedRecordings`) keeps shift=0 (it is not loop-aware) because its ghosts are removed and recreated by the next lifecycle tick anyway. Full suite green (12716); playtest pending.
  - **TODO (sibling, same playtest log): ~313ms wrong-position icon flash at TS entry for any looped mission member.** Same log captures the upstream cause: `CreateGhostVesselsFromCommittedRecordings` (the TS startup-create at `ParsekTrackingStation.cs:185` / `Patches/GhostTrackingStationPatch.cs:446`) iterates every committed recording at the RAW live `currentUT` (no `effUT` / no `loopEpochShift` plumbing), so for a loop member whose recording ended ~35M seconds before live, the source-resolve falls through to `EndpointTail` / `TerminalOrbit` and the create seeds an orbit at the recorded terminal position (off in empty space for a cross-body terminal). ~313ms later the lifecycle pass (`UpdateTrackingStationGhostLifecycle`) recomputes `effUT` via the span clock, finds `renderHidden=True` for the inter-cycle gap (or seeds the right segment for an in-cycle frame), and removes / replaces the wrong-position ghost. Net visual: every looped mission's icon briefly flashes at the wrong spot on TS entry, then settles. Not new; pre-dates the SOI-flicker fix. Fix shape: make the startup-create loop-aware — compute the per-index `effUT` via `GhostPlaybackLogic.ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT` + `cachedLoopUnits` (the lifecycle path already does this) and pass the matching `tsLoopEpochShift` into `CreateGhostVesselFromSource`. Skip loop members where `renderHidden=True` so the lifecycle handles them on the next tick instead of creating-then-removing. Likely small change; orthogonal to alignment-modes / zero-drift work.
  - **Prior-art note (cloned mods, `Code/Parsek/mods/`):** verified in-game 2026-05-27 (`PhaseLock APPLIED method=joint-best-fit P=1250859 (=9 Mun periods) residual=992.7s`, map icon `drawn>=1` in-window, zero `positionFailure` all run). Surveyed the two relevant cloned mods for reusable period math: **KerbalAlarmClock** (MIT; `Utilities.CurrentPhaseAngle`, `TimeObjects.CalcPhaseAngleTarget = 180*(1-((a_o+a_t)/(2*a_t))^1.5)`, `SharedStuff/AngleRenderPhase.cs`) computes the Hohmann DEPARTURE phase angle + synodic recurrence - i.e. the **re-aim** model ("when to fly a fresh transfer"), NOT our replay-as-is near-resonance; useful only if a re-aim mode is ever added (out of scope per the locked "replay as-is" decision). **KSTS** (`Source/MissionController.cs`) is purely timer-based (`eta = now + profile.missionDuration`, then teleport/assemble the payload) with NO phase/synodic math - relevant to logistics resource-flow, not to periodicity geometry. Conclusion: no cloned mod implements the multi-period near-coincidence we need; the zero-drift follow-up is a self-contained numerical method (continued-fraction / Stern-Brocot best-rational-approximation of the constraint period ratios). MechJebLib (public domain) + TransferWindowPlanner2 (MIT) are NOT cloned and not required for replay-as-is.
- **TODO - Phase 4: cross-parent / interplanetary (e.g. Duna), still `UnsupportedCrossParent` (deferred).** A sibling/interplanetary target is reported unsupported today (falls back to the raw anchor, never mis-scheduled). The clean replay-as-is extension reuses the Phase-2 joint best-fit: emit heliocentric `Orbital` constraints for BOTH the origin body (Kerbin) and the target body (Duna) around the shared parent (Sun) and let `FindBestJointMultiple` find the multi-period near-resonance (the dominant = the longest heliocentric period). The body-hierarchy walk to the common parent is already designed in the logistics doc (`docs/parsek-logistics-supply-routes-design.md` §8.1) and `IBodyInfo.ReferenceBodyName`/`OrbitPeriod` already expose the inputs. NOT the synodic period (that is the re-aim model). Interplanetary near-resonance periods are very long (the ghost is rare), so pair with the warp-to-window quick-win below.
- **quick win (done): "Warp to..." button on a looped mission row.** The recurring "the icon rarely appears" complaint is inherent to faithful inter-body cadence (one launch per ~14.5 days for the Mun). New `DrawMissionWarpToWindowButton` (after Delete, before Loop; `"Warp to..."` label per the existing convention, the adjacent TTL column says "to what") fast-forwards the clock to `RewindToLaunchLeadTimeSeconds` (15 s) before the mission's next relaunch (`periodicity.NextRelaunchUT`). **Playtest follow-up:** the first cut routed through `WarpToTimeController.RequestWarp` which, IN FLIGHT, did a full flight->Space-Center scene exit + reload (confirmed in the log: `Deferred flight warp ... returning to the Space Center`). Reworked to use the SAME in-place fast-forward as the Forward button (no scene change): `ShowMissionWarpToWindowConfirmation` -> in flight `ParsekFlight.FastForwardToEventUT(relaunchUT, label)` (new; applies `ApplyJumpLead`, `NotifyRecorder`, `TimeJumpManager.ExecuteForwardJump`), at the Space Center a direct `ExecuteForwardJump(ApplyJumpLead(...))`. Dropped the now-obsolete component machinery (`WarpToTimeMath.ComputeComponentsFromUT` + `MissionsWindowUI.RoundWarpTargetUpToMinute`, both added in the first cut, and their tests - `ExecuteForwardJump` takes a precise UT, so no minute-truncation round-trip is needed; the earlier review-fix for that truncation is moot). Enabled only when looping + an engine unit was built + the relaunch is finite and >1s in the future + the scene is warp-capable (flight or Space Center), via the pure `ShouldEnableWarpToWindow` (unit-tested). `ColW_PeriodLocked` trimmed 184->160 (still fits the longest basis label) to make room in the fixed-width header right block; Watch/Rewind stay column-stable (fixed-width button on every row). The `FastForwardToEventUT` / confirmation / IMGUI paths are runtime/playtest-verified.
- **mission title bubble spacing (done):** `missionHeaderRowStyle` padding was `(0,0,0,4)` (0 top, 4 bottom), leaving a visible extra band under the buttons/text inside the dark bubble (the gap above != below). Set to `(0,0,2,2)` (equal top/bottom) so the spacing is symmetric.
- **first-play floor (done):** a looped mission must never relaunch before its first real play (the original recording, `[spanStart, spanEnd]`, which spawns a real vessel at `spanEnd`) completes. `TryBuildMissionUnit` now clamps the phase anchor to at least `spanEndUT`: `baseAnchorUT = Math.Max(baseAnchorUT, spanEndUT)` (unlocked path) and `referenceUT = Math.Max(referenceUT, spanEndUT)` before `Solve`/`NextWindow` (phase-locked path - keeps the result a faithful `UT0 + k*P` window AND `>= spanEndUT`). The span clock (`TryComputeSpanLoopUT` / `ComputeNewestMissionInstanceSpanLoopUT`) already plays nothing before `phaseAnchorUT` and floors `missionCycle` at 0, so the anchor clamp is the whole fix. Normal flow (loop enabled after the recording, `LoopAnchorUT > spanEndUT`) is a no-op; this only bites a NaN anchor or a future-dated recording (e.g. after a career rewind, whose faithful window could otherwise fall before the launch via negative `k`). Updated `Build_NaNAnchor_*` (NaN now clamps to `spanEndUT`, not `spanStartUT`) + new `Build_LoopAnchorBeforeFirstPlay_ClampsAnchorToAfterTheFirstPlay` (both the locked faithful-window path and the unlocked direct-clamp path).

---

## TODO - v0.10.0 Missions: docking/undocking effect on mission structure (decision recorded, gaps deferred)

- **Decision (2026-05-26 design chat, recorded in `docs/dev/design-mission-abstractions.md` "Docking & undocking (v1)"):** dock / undock affect the mission structure ONLY as tree topology (the existing Dock/Board merge + Undock fork branch points). NO Mission-entity lifecycle is auto-created/closed on dock/undock; loopable segments are interval-level Mission selections over that topology. "Main controller A or B" is not a choice we impose - the docked stack has one KSP active controller and the combined leg records into its tree.
- **Verified loopable today:** A-solo / B-solo (pre-dock), A-after / B-after undock (undock is a structural peel so the line splits + the departing vessel is its own offshoot), peeled offshoots, and a whole-vessel journey. Audited against `MissionLoopUnitBuilder` (drives looping from `Mission.ExcludedIntervalKeys` via `MissionIntervalSelection`) + `MissionCompositionBuilder` (intervals split at structural peels).
- **Gaps (DEFERRED until after supply-routes v0 integration; do NOT fix yet):**
  1. **Dock is not an interval boundary.** `MissionCompositionBuilder.BuildNode` edges only at structural-peel UTs (children leaving), never at a Dock/Board merge UT (a vessel joining), so the docked "AB" stretch is lumped into the continuing vessel's pre-dock interval and can't be looped in isolation. Fix sketch: emit a merge-UT edge on the continuing line when its controller count increases.
  2. **Docked composition understated.** Interval composition = head start composition MINUS structural peels; it never ADDS controllers gained at a dock, and a later undock peel subtracts the departing vessel's parts that were never in the head count (clamped at 0). Tied to gap 1.
  3. ~~**Undock continuation vs offshoot is non-deterministic.**~~ DONE. `ContinuationSuccessor` now honors the recorder's `BranchPoint.ChildRecordingIds[0]` convention (the continuing/active vessel, or the single merged Dock/Board child): `MissionStructureBuilder` marks that leg `MissionLeg.IsBranchContinuation` (derived, not serialized) and `MissionThroughLineBuilder.ContinuationSuccessor` prefers it among the children that already pass its non-anchored/non-EVA filter, so an undock fork's main line follows the controlled vessel instead of a GUID tiebreak. No schema change. Validated by `MissionStructureTests` (`BranchContinuation_IsMarkedOnFirstChild_OfForkAndMerge`, `UndockFork_ContinuationFollowsActiveChild_NotGuidTiebreak`) plus the existing decouple/EVA/dock cases (anchored/EVA children are filtered before the preference, so they are unaffected).
  4. **Cross-tree (foreign-vessel) dock.** Combined leg + post-undock continuation land in the controller's tree while the foreign partner's pre-dock flight stays in its own tree, so "loop the whole shared docked journey from the foreign side" spans two trees. Remaining half of design-doc open question 6; revisit with cross-tree dock-link following (PID-linking like `GhostChainWalker`).

---

## Done - v0.10.0 In-game test failures from the 2026-05-28 run (foreground monotonicity, restore-guard leak, dialog cascade, partless markers)

Four distinct in-game test failures from the 2026-05-28 batch run, root-caused and fixed.

- **`CommittedRecordingsHaveValidData` (all scenes): non-monotonic flat `Recording.Points`.** Recording `f1d2e5fc...` had `Points[2].ut 60.9327 < Points[1].ut 61.3727` (a 0.44s backwards step), source=Active. Root cause: the #419 monotonicity reject was added only to the BACKGROUND recorder (`BackgroundRecorder.ApplyTrajectoryPointToRecording`); the FOREGROUND commit path (`FlightRecorder.CommitRecordedPointWithVessel` / `...WithoutVessel`) only had the large-regression (`>= TimeRegressionThresholdSeconds = 1.0s`) quickload/revert trim, so a sub-1s backwards step (a stale-UT seam point at a RELATIVE->Absolute section handoff, dual-written into the flat list and `TrackSection.frames`) slipped through. Fix: new pure `FlightRecorder.ClassifyForegroundCommitTimeOrder(count, pointUT, lastRecordedUT)` (Append / TrimThenAppend / RejectNonMonotonic); both foreground commit methods now reject a sub-threshold regression instead of appending it. Plus load-time defense-in-depth: `TrajectoryTextSidecarCodec.DropNonMonotonicTrajectoryPoints` (wrapped by `RecordingStore`) drops any backwards flat point on load (both `TrajectorySidecarBinary.ReadBinaryTrajectoryFile` and `DeserializeTrajectoryFrom`), so a recording already saved with the corruption loads clean. Not version-gated (universal invariant, mirrors the existing `AppendPointsFromTrackSections` #419 guard), not a format migration. Tests: `ForegroundMonotonicityTests` (12).
- **`ReentrancyGuard_ClearedAfterRestore` (FLIGHT): static `ParsekFlight.restoringActiveTree` stuck true.** The #267 restore coroutines set the static guard true and clear it in a `finally`, but Unity abandons a running coroutine when the MonoBehaviour is destroyed on a scene change WITHOUT running the `finally`, so a mid-restore scene exit left the static flag stuck true and the next scene's fresh `ParsekFlight` inherited it. Fix: clear `restoringActiveTree = false` in `ParsekFlight.OnDestroy` (the next scene re-schedules its own restore, so clearing is always safe). The existing in-game test is the regression guard.
- **`OnFlightReady_NoReFlySession_ShowsMergeDialog` (FLIGHT): merge dialog timed out (cascade of the above).** `ShouldShowOnFlightReadyMergeDialog` requires `!restoringActiveTree`; with the guard leaked true the control's dialog was silently suppressed. Fixed by the `OnDestroy` clear above. Also added an explicit `restoringActiveTree == false` precondition assert in the control test so a future regression points at the guard instead of timing out opaquely.
- **`GhostMarkerProtoVesselsHaveHardenedPartTolerances` (TRACKSTATION): stale test, vessels=2 parts=0.** Ghost map markers are kept on-rails (unloaded) by `GhostVesselLoadPatch` blocking `Vessel.GoOffRails`, so KSP never instantiates live `Part` objects (`v.parts` empty) in the Tracking Station; the live-Part aero/thermal hardening (`HardenGhostVesselPartPhysics`) has nothing to act on, so the `checkedParts > 0` assertion could never pass. Fix: the test now treats "marker found but no live parts" as not-applicable (logs and returns) instead of failing; the per-part +Inf assertions still fire for any marker that did instantiate live parts. FOLLOW-UP (open): in TRACKSTATION the test now never exercises the hardening (markers are always unloaded there). Real coverage of "a marker that enters physics range during a low-altitude Re-Fly cannot explode" needs a FLIGHT-scene test that forces a ghost map marker off-rails (or asserts at the live-Part level once one loads). The ProtoPartSnapshot is deliberately unhardened (BuildGhostProtoVesselNode), so asserting on snapshot tolerances is not an alternative.

---

## Done - v0.10.0 Recordings tab: hide Loop checkbox + period on debris rows and debris-only groups

- Player request (2026-05-28): "hide the loop checkbox and period objects for debris recordings and debris group in the Recordings window; make sure that if a parent recording has loop enabled, then the debris is part of that as a child animation which plays at the right time; this is already done in Missions window, where debris is not even shown, but we should unify this behavior and add it to recordings window also."
- **Parent-anchored debris already plays in sync with its parent's loop clock** (`GhostPlaybackEngine.TryUpdateLoopSyncedDebris`, `GhostPlaybackEngine.cs:1681`): when the parent has `LoopPlayback=true` (or is a Mission loop-unit member), the debris recording is dispatched onto the parent's loop UT + parent-unit overlap cadence, including the start-/end-trim window. So a separate per-debris loop toggle does nothing the engine reads; surfacing it just suggested control that did not exist.
- **UI fix (`RecordingsTableUI`):** new pure helpers + four call sites updated:
  - `ShouldSuppressRowLoopUi(rec, insideUnfinishedFlightsGroup)`: returns true when the per-row Loop/Period cells should render as empty width-stable placeholders. Two cases: the existing Unfinished Flights virtual group (preserved verbatim), and `rec.IsDebris` (new). `DrawRecordingRow` reads this once and uses the same boolean for both the Loop and the Period cell.
  - `ComputeLoopAggregate(committed[, indices])`: pure aggregate state for a group/chain/header row. Excludes debris members from both the count and the "all loop" decision and reports `SuppressToggle=true` when the only members are debris (so the auto-generated `"<mission> / Debris"` subgroup, and any custom group that happens to hold only debris, render an empty Loop cell instead of a no-op aggregate toggle). Header overload (no `indices` parameter) walks `committed` with a plain `for` loop to avoid an `Enumerable.Range` iterator allocation on every OnGUI repaint. `LoopAggregateState.AllLoop` and `SuppressToggle` are read-only properties computed from the two count inputs, so a constructed state cannot drift from its counts.
  - `BulkSetLoopPlayback(committed, indices, value, applyAutoRange)`: shared bulk-write helper. Header / group / `select-all` paths call it with `applyAutoRange=false` so `LoopStartUT`/`LoopEndUT` are never touched, and chain / grouped-block paths call it with `applyAutoRange=true` to preserve the pre-existing per-row auto-narrow behavior. Debris and out-of-range indices are skipped, returning the count actually written for the log line.
  - Used in `DrawGroupTree`, `DrawRecordingBlock` (chains + grouped blocks), and the column-header "select-all Loop" toggle. Bulk-write paths all skip debris so the header / group / chain aggregate writes stay consistent with the per-row hide.
  - **Pre-existing asymmetry preserved on purpose:** the chain/block bulk-write and the per-row toggle call `ApplyAutoLoopRange` (auto-narrows the loop window when flipping on, clears it on flip-off); the header and group bulk-writes do not (so the user can flip a group's aggregate Loop off then back on without losing a manually-customized `LoopStartUT/LoopEndUT` on any member). The refactor briefly added `ApplyAutoLoopRange` to `DrawGroupTree` (Opus review flagged this as scope creep that would clobber custom ranges); reverted to match the original behavior, then expressed by routing all four call sites through `BulkSetLoopPlayback(applyAutoRange)`. Pinned by `BulkSetLoopPlayback_GroupMode_DoesNotTouchCustomRange` and `BulkSetLoopPlayback_ChainMode_AppliesAutoRange`.
  - **Load-time debris sanitization (`ParsekScenario.SanitizeDebrisLoopPlayback`):** OnLoad sweep clears stale `LoopPlayback=true` on any `IsDebris=true` recording (warn-log with cleared count). Pre-PR saves with stale debris loop flags now get cleaned at load instead of requiring the user to find the Timeline `L` button. Idempotent on subsequent loads (no cleared rows once already swept).
- **Mirrors the Missions tab**, which already excludes debris entirely from its composition tree (no `IsDebris` reads in `MissionComposition`/`MissionLoopUnitBuilder`/`MissionStore`). The Recordings tab still surfaces debris as rows (it is the flat list), but hides only the controls that would have been inert.
- **Tests:** 18 new `RecordingsTableUITests` covering the helpers: `ShouldSuppressRowLoopUi_*` (normal row, debris row, Unfinished Flights group, debris-in-Unfinished-Flights, null defensive), `ComputeLoopAggregate_*` (all non-debris loop, mixed, debris excluded, all debris suppresses toggle, empty, out-of-range indices skipped, null collections), `ComputeLoopAggregateHeader_*` (header overload parity with the indexed overload, null/empty), `LoopAggregateState_DerivedProperties_NeverDriftFromCounts`, `BulkSetLoopPlayback_*` (group-mode does not touch custom range, chain-mode applies auto-range, skips debris, skips null/out-of-range, returns written count). Plus 3 new `RecordingStoreTests` for `SanitizeDebrisLoopPlayback` (clears stale flags, idempotent, leaves non-debris rows alone).
- **Model-layer defense (`IPlaybackTrajectory.LoopPlayback`):** the interface getter now returns `!IsDebris && LoopPlayback` so any future code path that sets `LoopPlayback=true` on a debris recording without going through `BulkSetLoopPlayback` (which skips debris) still reads as `false` at the engine boundary. With `SanitizeDebrisLoopPlayback` running at every OnLoad and every existing `IsDebris=true` setter creating fresh recordings (BackgroundRecorder decouple) or copying from a recording whose `LoopPlayback` was already sanitized (RecordingOptimizer split, SessionMerger, RewindInvoker, codec load), this collapses to a no-op in practice. The masking is belt-and-braces. Pinned by `IPlaybackTrajectory_LoopPlayback_MasksDebris` in `RecordingsTableUITests`.
- **Timeline tab L button on debris:** with the above two mechanisms in place (load-time sanitization + model-layer mask), `TimelineWindowUI.ShouldShowLoopToggle` reliably does not surface the `L` on debris. The predicate is still debris-naive on its face (`LoopPlayback || IsLoopableRecording(rec)`), but `IsLoopableRecording` already returns false for debris, and the `LoopPlayback` half is now closed by the load-time sweep plus the model-layer guard.
- **Known follow-up not in this PR:** Controlled-decoupled children (`IsDebris=false`, `ParentAnchorRecordingId != null`) also ride the parent loop clock per the parent-anchored contract; this PR's hide predicate only filters `IsDebris`, leaving the Loop UI visible on those children. Different schema cell, different test surface, properly scoped as a future PR.
- **Status:** CLOSED 2026-05-28.

## Done - v0.10.0 Missions window: Archive column (long-list management)

- Player request: a way to deal with long mission lists, copying the recordings window's Archive mechanism.
- **Mechanism (mirrors `RecordingsTableUI` + `GroupHierarchyStore.HideActive`):** new `Mission.Archived` per-mission flag + new global `MissionStore.HideArchived` toggle. The Missions window gained a rightmost `Archive` column: the column header carries the global toggle (label "Archive" + a checkbox bound to `HideArchived`), and each mission row carries its own `Archived` checkbox (after Delete). When `HideArchived` is on, the draw loop skips archived missions (`if (MissionStore.HideArchived && mission.Archived) continue;`). Composition rows get an empty trailing `ColW_Archive` cell (a margin-0 `BeginHorizontal` container, see the alignment-polish entry below) so their right edge lines up with the header.
- **Scope:** archiving is purely list visibility, like a recording's `Hidden`. It does NOT touch looping or ghost playback (the loop unit is still built from all `MissionStore.Missions`); an archived-but-looping mission keeps looping until you turn Loop off. Un-archive or toggle the header off to see it again.
- **Persistence:** `Mission.Save/Load` round-trip `archived`; `MissionStore.Save/Load` round-trip `missionHideArchived`. `Clone` copies `Archived`. `ResetForTesting` clears `HideArchived`. Missing values (older saves) default to not-archived / toggle-off.
- **Window size persistence (SUPERSEDED by the tab merge below):** the standalone Missions window used to remember its size via `MissionStore.WindowWidth`/`WindowHeight` (NaN = unset, round-tripped through `Save`/`Load` as `missionWindowWidth`/`missionWindowHeight`), restored in `MissionsWindowUI.DrawIfOpen`. After Missions became a tab inside the Recordings window, that window no longer exists; `DrawIfOpen` was removed and the `WindowWidth/Height` fields are now inert (see "Missions is a tab in the Recordings window" -> Known dead state).
- **Tests:** 4 new `MissionStoreTests` (archived + HideArchived round-trip; missing values default off; Clone copies Archived; window-size round-trip + unset-stays-NaN). Full suite green (12560).
- **Status:** CLOSED 2026-05-25.

## Done - v0.10.0 Missions window: header/column alignment + Loop checkbox polish

- Three playtest-reported UI polish items in `MissionsWindowUI` (2026-05-26):
  1. **Vessel rows' columns drifted ~4px left of their headers.** Confirmed against the captured `skin margins` diagnostic (`box`/`label`/`toggle`/`button`/`textField` all margin L4/R4) + the `AlignDbg HEADER` rects: every skin style has margin 4, but a bare `BeginHorizontal` (`GUIStyle.none`) has margin 0. The header's rightmost Archive cell is a margin-0 `BeginHorizontal`, while the composition rows' trailing Archive cell was a margin-4 `bodyCellLabel` Label. The LAST cell's right margin sets where the whole right-side column block sits relative to the scrollbar (the expanding "Missions and vessels" column absorbs everything to the left, so right columns position from the right), so the body's extra 4px right margin pushed every time/event column ~4px left of its header. Fix: the composition row's trailing Archive cell is now a margin-0 `BeginHorizontal(Width(ColW_Archive))` + `FlexibleSpace` container, matching both the column header and the mission-header row's Archive cell. Other fixed columns (StartTime/StartEvent/EndEvent/EndTime) already aligned (header box margin 4 == body `bodyCellLabel` margin 4). (Follow-up 2026-05-26: widened `ColW_StartTime` and `ColW_EndTime` 100 -> 120 for a bit more room; both header and body read the same constant so alignment is preserved.)
  2. **Archive header dark cell did not wrap its checkbox.** The header applied the dark box style (`colHdr`) to the "Archive" LABEL only, so the checkbox sat outside the box. Fix: mirror `RecordingsTableUI` - new `colHdrCellContainerStyle` (clone of the shared column-header box with L/R margin zeroed so its footprint stays exactly `Width(ColW_Archive)`) on the cell's `BeginHorizontal`, plus a plain bold `boldHeaderInnerLabel` inside (boxing it again would double-box), so the dark box spans label + checkbox. (Follow-up 2026-05-26: bumped `ColW_Archive` 60 -> 80 to equal `RecordingsTableUI.ColW_Hide` so the Archive column reads the same width on both the Recordings and Missions tabs.)
  3. **Per-mission Loop toggle read "[x] Loop".** `Toggle(value, "Loop")` renders checkbox-then-label. Fix: render a "Loop" label then a bare `Toggle(value, "")` inside a `BeginHorizontal(Width(ColW_Loop))` (label-then-checkbox, "Loop [x]"), mirroring the recordings "Loop" select-all header; bumped `ColW_Loop` 52->64 so both fit side by side (`ColW_Loop` lives on the header row only, so widening it just shrinks the expanding title slightly).
- UI-rendering-only (no new logic methods, no schema, no changed signatures), so no new unit tests; full suite still green (12585). Built + deployed, DLL verified at the real running-KSP path (size 4540416; the worktree build's `..\..\..` copy target resolves to the main repo `Parsek/`). The dead `DrawThroughLine*`/`DrawReferenceRow` render methods were left untouched (still only self-recursive, never called from `DrawWindow`).
- **Status:** CLOSED 2026-05-26.

## Done - v0.10.0 Missions is a tab in the Recordings window (not a separate window)

- Player request (2026-05-26): access the Missions view as a second tab inside the Recordings window (two equal-width tabs across the top, like the Kerbals window), each a way to view + loop the same recordings, structured differently (Recordings = flat grouped/chained list; Missions = mission structure). Decisions: single "Recordings" main-panel button (no separate "Missions" button); one shared window width (no resize on tab switch).
- **Host (`RecordingsTableUI`):** `DrawRecordingsWindow` now draws `GUILayout.Toolbar(selectedTab, {"Recordings","Missions"}, toggleButtonStyle)` (the standard 2-segment toolbar = each half width) below the title, logs `LogTabSwitch(old,new)` on change, then dispatches. Tab 0 = the existing recordings body verbatim (its own `DrawRecordingsBottomBar` keeps Info / New Group / Close + resize + DragWindow + tooltip). Tab 1 early-returns after `parentUI.GetMissionsUI().DrawMissionsTabContent()` + a slim `DrawMissionsTabBottomBar` (shared Close + resize + DragWindow; no Info/New Group). New fields `selectedTab`/`TabRecordings`/`TabMissions`/`TabLabels` + `toggleButtonStyle` (built in `EnsurePhaseStyles`, the active-background "pressed" idiom from KerbalsWindowUI/CareerStateWindowUI). `EnsurePhaseStyles` is called at the top of `DrawRecordingsWindow` so the tab style exists before the toolbar. `selectedTab` is transient (survives close/reopen, resets to Recordings on a fresh session) and not persisted.
- **`MissionsWindowUI` window -> tab content drawer:** dropped all window chrome (`showWindow`/`IsOpen`, `windowRect`/`lastWindowRect`/`isResizing`/`hasInputLock`, `InputLockId`/`MinWindowWidth`/`MinWindowHeight`/`DefaultWidth`, `DrawIfOpen`, `ReleaseInputLock`, the `ClickThruBlocker.GUILayoutWindow` wrapper, the resize/drag, the per-frame input lock, and the `MissionStore.WindowWidth/Height` reads+writes). `DrawWindow(int)` became `internal DrawMissionsTabContent()`: defocus-commit check + column header + scroll list (no outer vertical, no Close, no resize/drag), mirroring the recordings tab's header-plus-scroll shape so the host's bottom bar pins below it. Kept `scrollPos` (the tab's own scroll), all styles, caches, rename state, and every `Draw*` helper. `using ClickThroughFix;` dropped.
- **Wiring (`ParsekUI` / `ParsekFlight` / `ParsekKSC`):** removed the "Missions" main-panel button and the `DrawMissionsWindowIfOpen` method + its two call sites (flight + KSC); added `internal MissionsWindowUI GetMissionsUI()`. The `missionsUI` instance is still constructed by ParsekUI (it owns the tab content). The recordings window's input lock + mouse-over now cover the merged window, so the Missions tab no longer needs its own. Neither tab shows at the Tracking Station (unchanged: the recordings window was never drawn there).
- **Known dead state (follow-up, not fixed here):** `MissionStore.WindowWidth/Height` (+ their `missionWindowWidth/Height` persistence and the `MissionStoreTests` round-trip test) are now unread by the UI (the merged window uses the recordings window's size, which is not persisted). Left inert (Save only emits them when set, and nothing sets them now) to keep this change focused; remove with the persistence + test in a later cleanup if desired.
- **Follow-up polish (2026-05-26):** (1) the mission header row now draws the dark section-header box as the background of the WHOLE row (new `missionHeaderRowStyle` = section-header box with L/R margin+padding zeroed so the bubble spans edge to edge without insetting the contents); the index + title moved off their own `GetSectionHeaderStyle()` boxes to a bold transparent `missionHeaderTextStyle` so they sit on the bubble instead of double-boxing. (2) `RecordingsTableUI.MinWindowWidth` raised from 350 to `DefaultCollapsedWindowWidth` (the Recordings table's collapsed/Info-off width) so neither tab can be dragged narrow enough to clip the Recordings columns; it is a single shared clamp (`DrawIfOpen` -> `HandleResizeDrag`), so the Missions tab was already bounded by the same minimum, this just raises that minimum to a usable value. Expanding Info still widens the window to `DefaultExpandedWindowWidth`.
- **Follow-up polish 2 (2026-05-26):** (1) `missionHeaderRowStyle` ALL margins + padding zeroed (was keeping the section-header's top/bottom 4/4), so the bubble adds no extra vertical height and the mission header rows line up with the Recordings tab's row spacing (the Recordings group header is a plain unboxed `BeginHorizontal`). (2) `DrawMissionHeader` reordered: Clone + Delete now sit just right of the expanding title, to the LEFT of the Loop control. (3) New Rewind/Forward cell right of Watch: `RecordingsTableUI.DrawLegacyRewindForwardCell` made `internal` and reused for the mission's root recording (new `MissionsWindowUI.ResolveMissionRootRecordingIndex` = earliest-StartUT committed member across all of the mission's through-lines; passes that recording + committed index, or null -> blank `ColW_Rewind` cell). Final header order: index | title(expand) | Clone | Delete | Loop[x] | period | Watch | R/FF | Archive. The R/FF cell shows in flight + KSC (like Recordings); `[ERS-exempt]` (raw committed index, same as the watch button). The `TemporalButtons_RemainIndependentFromWatchState_PinnedBySourceInspection` source-inspection test anchor updated `private`->`internal` for the now-internal helper (the watch-state-independence invariant it pins is unchanged). Full suite green (12586).
- **Follow-up polish 3 (2026-05-26): Re-Fly column on the Missions tab.** New `ColW_ReFly = 90` column with a `"Re-Fly"` header to the LEFT of Archive (`DrawColumnHeader`), and a per-vessel Fly / Seal cell on the composition rows: `RecordingsTableUI.DrawReFlyColumnCell` made `internal` and reused (it shows Fly / Seal only for unfinished-flight recordings, else a blank `ColW_ReFly` cell). The composition row resolves its recording via new `MissionsWindowUI.TryResolveCommittedRecording(node.HeadLegId, ...)` (linear committed lookup, `[ERS-exempt]`, file allowlisted); only NON-atom rows resolve (atoms inherit the parent's HeadLegId and would duplicate the button) - atoms + unresolved rows draw a blank `ColW_ReFly` cell so the Archive column stays aligned. `GUI.color` is restored to normal BEFORE the Re-Fly cell so an excluded (greyed) interval's Fly / Seal buttons are not dimmed (re-fly state is independent of loop inclusion). The mission header bar is unchanged (it is a distinct bar; only its Archive must stay right-aligned, which it does). The same source-inspection test's end-anchor updated `private`->`internal void DrawReFlyColumnCell`. Composition rows align because the Re-Fly cell is inserted before the margin-0 Archive cell in both header and rows. Full suite green (12586).
- **Follow-up polish 4 (2026-05-26): header heights + uniform header-bar buttons.** (1) New `ColHeaderHeight = 32` (matches RecordingsTableUI) forced on every Missions column-header cell (`GUILayout.Height` on each label + the Archive container; the sortable headers take it via `DrawSortableHeaderCore`'s height param), so the toggle-bearing Archive header no longer makes the band uneven. (2) New `ColW_HeaderButton = 70` (old Clone width 60 + 10) replaces `ColW_Action` + `ColW_Watch` (both removed) for the mission-header-bar Clone / Delete / Watch buttons, so they read as one button group. (3) The mission-header Rewind/Forward button now renders via new `RecordingsTableUI.DrawMissionRewindForwardButton` (internal): a plain fixed-width (`ColW_HeaderButton`) button labelled "Rewind" / "Forward" instead of the `DrawLegacyRewindForwardCell` centered "R" / "FF" cell - this also fixes the oversized Watch->Rewind gap (the legacy cell's `BodyCellButtonLeftInset` added extra space; the plain button collapses to the same 4px margin as Clone->Delete). It reuses the SAME `ShouldShowForwardButton`/`ShouldShowLegacyRewindButton` + `RecordingStore.CanRewind`/`CanFastForward` + `ShowRewindConfirmation`/`ShowFastForwardConfirmation` logic, so behaviour is identical to the recordings R/FF (just the rendering differs). Body cell vertical text/spacing already matched (both tabs use the same `bodyCellLabel`). `DrawLegacyRewindForwardCell` stays `internal` (now only called by the recordings tab) so the source-inspection test anchor is unaffected. Full suite green (12586).
- **Follow-up polish 5 (2026-05-26): first-column / name-column alignment between tabs.** The Missions first column was a single `ColW_Index` (30) cell; the Recordings first column is a merged `[enable + index]` cell (`Width(ColW_Enable + ColW_Index + 8)`), so the Missions "Missions and vessels" column started ~20 px left of the Recordings "Name" column. Fixed by mirroring the Recordings first-column structure: added `ColW_Enable = 20`; the Missions "#" header is now a merged `colHdrCellContainerStyle` cell `Width(ColW_Enable + ColW_Index + 8)` with a blank enable slot + the sortable "#" inline (`boldHeaderInnerLabel`, manual sort like the recordings inline "#"); and a blank `ColW_Enable` cell now precedes the index (mission header bar) and the include checkbox (composition rows). Because the first-column block is built identically to the recordings tab, the expanding name column starts at the same x in both tabs. The include checkbox now sits in the index slot (under "#"). The inline "#" sort arrows are written as Unicode escapes (U+25B2 / U+25BC) to keep the source ASCII, matching `DrawSortableHeaderCore`. Full suite green (12586).
- **Follow-up polish 6 (2026-05-26): even spacing around the Loop checkbox.** The "Loop" label + checkbox were wrapped in `BeginHorizontal(Width(ColW_Loop=64))`, which was wider than the content (~52 px), so the ~12 px slack appeared as an oversized gap after the checkbox before the period field. Removed the fixed-width wrapper (and the now-unused `ColW_Loop` const): the "Loop" label and the toggle are emitted as bare siblings, so each side gets the normal ~4 px margin like the rest of the header row. Full suite green (12585 + the environmental `InjectAllRecordings` skip-as-failure while KSP holds KSP.log).
- **Follow-up polish 7 (2026-05-26): composition row height for the Fly/Seal buttons.** The composition (vessel) rows are mostly plain `bodyCellLabel` cells, which alone measure shorter than a recordings-table row, so the rows packed too tightly and left no room for the per-row Re-Fly Fly / Seal button. Added `CompositionRowMinHeight = 22f` (the recordings table's per-row scroll stride, `recordingsScrollPos.y = row * 22f`) as a `GUILayout.MinHeight` on the composition row's `BeginHorizontal`, so every vessel row is at least a recordings-row tall and the Fly / Seal button fits. Full suite green (12586).
- **Follow-up polish 8 (2026-05-26): mission title bar layout.** Three fixes in `DrawMissionHeader`: (1) `missionHeaderRowStyle` gained `padding.bottom = 4` so the title text has breathing room under it (top space comes from the box border). (2) A `GUILayout.Space(BodyCellTextIndent)` before the title so its text starts at the same inset as the "Missions and vessels" column-header text (the header box insets its label; the bare title label did not). (3) The right-side controls (Clone, Delete, Loop, period, Watch, Rewind, FlexibleSpace, Archive) are now wrapped in a fixed-width `BeginHorizontal(Width(MissionHeaderRightBlockWidth))`, where `MissionHeaderRightBlockWidth = ColW_StartTime + ColW_StartEvent + ColW_EndEvent + ColW_EndTime + ColW_ReFly + ColW_Archive + 5*4` (the data columns' total footprint incl. 5 inter-cell margins). Because that block is the LAST element after the expanding title, the title now fills exactly the data rows' name-column width and the buttons begin at the data-column boundary (where "Start time" starts) instead of being pushed to the far right by the over-wide expanding title; the in-block FlexibleSpace pins Archive to the right (under the Archive header). One outer expander (title) + one in-block expander (FlexibleSpace) sit in separate layout scopes, so they don't fight. The +5*4 margin term is an estimate; nudge `MissionHeaderRightBlockWidth` if the buttons land a few px off the column boundary. Full suite green (12586).
- **Mission loop-period field stopped committing (regression from the header restructure, fixed 2026-05-26).** Playtest: typing a period then pressing Enter / clicking away no longer accepted the value. Root cause: `DrawMissionLoopPeriodCell` used a fragile commit-on-EVERY-keystroke path gated on `GUI.GetNameOfFocusedControl() == controlName` recomputed each frame; once today's header restructure (Clone/Delete reorder, the fixed-width right block, the Loop bare-siblings) destabilized the field's GUILayout keyboard-control id, `focused` flickered false, the per-frame buffer reseed clobbered the typed text, and nothing committed. The period-cell body itself was unchanged (last touched in `a7781c9d`/`37dbf3a2`); the breakage was indirect. Fix: rewrote it to mirror `RecordingsTableUI.DrawLoopPeriodCell`'s ROBUST mechanism - a single `loopPeriodFocusedMissionId` + `loopPeriodEditText` + `loopPeriodEditRect`, enter edit mode on focus-gain, then COMMIT on Enter (KeyDown, before the TextField consumes it) and on click-away (window-level MouseDown outside `loopPeriodEditRect`, handled in `DrawMissionsTabContent`), via new `CommitMissionLoopPeriodEdit` / `FindMissionById`. No longer depends on per-frame focus staying stable after focus-gain. Edit focus is cleared on unit-cycle, on Auto, and on loop-off. Removed the old `loopPeriodEditBuffers` dict. Runtime IMGUI path, playtest-validated; full suite green (12586).
- **Opus review pass (2026-05-26): UI + backend reviews, 4 items fixed.** Two clean-context Opus reviewers (one UI, one backend) reviewed PR #958. No blockers. Fixed: (1) **[Major]** `GhostPlaybackEngine.LogUnitTransitionIfChanged` picked the camera-live member and computed `watchedIsRendering` from RAW `traj.StartUT/EndUT` while `DecideUnitMemberRender` uses the unit's TRIMMED member window, so with interval-trim + watch the camera could hand off to / hold on a member the engine was hiding; now uses `unit.MemberStartUT/MemberEndUT(idx, ...)` for the scan + the watched-render check (and the hide diagnostic logs the trimmed bounds). (2) **[Minor]** `MissionStore.ReconcileSelections` only pruned stale `ExcludedThroughLineHeadIds`; now also prunes stale `ExcludedIntervalKeys` (builds the composition once per tree, drops keys absent from the selectable-node `HeadLegId` set) so a stale `/segN` key after a topology change can't silently mis-target a different segment - extracted a shared `RemoveStale` helper; +1 `MissionStoreTests`. (3) **[Minor/UI]** deleted the dead through-line renderer cluster in `MissionsWindowUI` (`DrawThroughLine`/`DrawThroughLineRow`/`DrawReferenceRow`/`StartEventText`/`EndEventText`/`EventLabel`, ~175 lines, zero callers) + the now-orphaned `MergeArrow` glyph. (4) **[Minor/UI]** removed the inert `MissionStore.WindowWidth/Height` (fields + Save/Load + ResetForTesting + the round-trip test); Save still purges the retired `missionWindowWidth/Height` keys from older saves. Reviewer-flagged-but-kept (per user): the 10s default loop period that self-overlaps long missions (matches the per-recording default; opt out by raising the period). Full suite green (12585 + the environmental `InjectAllRecordings` skip while KSP holds KSP.log).
- **Follow-up polish 9 (2026-05-26): vertically center the composition row content.** After flooring the composition rows at `CompositionRowMinHeight` (polish 7), the cells (content-height, top-aligned by GUILayout) floated at the top of the taller row with an empty gap below, unlike the recordings rows (whose buttons fill the row). New `compositionCellLabel` (clone of `bodyCellLabel` with `alignment = MiddleLeft` + `stretchHeight = true`) is now used for the vessel name button/label and the time/event labels, so they fill the row height and center their text vertically; the include checkbox toggle gets `GUILayout.ExpandHeight(true)` so it fills the row and the toggle style centers it. Net: the checkbox + name (+ time text) sit vertically centered in the row, matching how the recordings rows read. Full suite green (12586).
- **Tests:** +1 `RecordingsTableUITests.LogTabSwitch_Logs_OldAndNew` (log contract for the tab-switch helper). UI-rendering otherwise (IMGUI dispatch / layout, playtest-validated). Full suite green (12586). Built + deployed, DLL verified at the real running-KSP path (size 4539904, mtime matches build; new `Missions tab: missions=` string present).
